Current Commentary

British Empire Diplomatic Discussions and the Far Eastern Question 14

— Star

Recently, the Prime Ministers of the British Empire's self-governing dominions gathered in London on the occasion of the 25th anniversary of the ascension of the British monarch. They discussed the future diplomatic strategies of the Empire. According to Reuters, the discussions were of great significance, and the representatives of the self-governing dominions and the British cabinet had reached a consensus. Concrete decisions were also made on the defense of the Empire. These talks have a profound impact on the future of the Far East. Although we cannot know the exact conclusions, based on the usual statements of the leaders of the British Empire's dominions, the recent trends in the foreign policies of the self-governing dominions, and the current changes in the Pacific situation, the outcome of these talks is not difficult to surmise.

Those unfamiliar with the inner workings of the British Empire often confuse the British Empire with the London government. In reality, the traditional policies and current needs of the London government often do not align with the traditional policies and current needs of the various dominions. After the Great War, the dominions sent troops to Europe to assist the London government, so the London government gradually considered the wishes of the dominions and respected their opinions in foreign and defense matters. At the Paris Peace Conference, the dominions had representatives. In the League of Nations, the delegations of the dominions held equal status with the British delegation. At the 1921 Imperial Conference, when discussing the abolition or continuation of the Anglo-Japanese Alliance, Canadian Prime Minister Meighen single-handedly overturned the pro-Japanese and anti-American policy decided by the London government. He proposed that the United States, Great Britain, China, and Japan hold a joint conference to resolve the Far Eastern disputes. At the time, even conservatives like Foreign Secretary Curzon changed their plans to safeguard the overall interests of the Empire and accepted his proposal. Therefore, the Imperial Conference of June 1921 was actually a precursor to the Washington Conference. Without the efforts of the Canadian representative, relations between Great Britain and the United States would have deteriorated, and the Anglo-Japanese Alliance, the Nine-Power Treaty, and the Four-Power Treaty would not have been produced. The ten years of uneasy peace in the Pacific would not have been possible. At that time, if the London government's opinion had prevailed, the United States would have refused the League of Nations and humiliated Great Britain, and international credibility would have been lost. Cooperation would have been impossible. Japan, having allied with Great Britain since 1902, had been a powerful ally in the Far East for ten years, and there was a need to continue the alliance. However, Great Britain's willingness to cooperate with the United States at the Washington Conference was due to the success of the foreign policies of the dominions and the London government's acceptance of their opinions.

The reasons why the London government was pro-Japanese and the dominion governments were pro-American have their own geographical and historical causes and are not accidental. Great Britain's traditional foreign policy has been to maintain the security of the English Channel. Therefore, it is willing to pursue anything that is beneficial to maintaining the balance of power on the continent and its maritime hegemony. Its willingness to connect with Japan was to alleviate its concerns in the east, allowing it to cope with the European continent with more ease. Furthermore, Great Britain also needed Japan's assistance against Russia and Germany. However, the politicians of the dominions thought differently. They had little interest in European issues and did not consider the safety of the English Channel to be of immediate concern to them. What worried them was the declining strength of the British Navy. Australia, New Zealand, Canada, and South Africa are thousands of miles away from London. The British Navy and Air Force are insufficient to guarantee their security. This is one reason. After the Great War, Japan rose in the Far East. Its naval power could move south and threaten Australia and New Zealand, and eastwards, it could endanger Canada. Moreover, its economic aggression was very fierce. South Africa, Australia, Canada, and other places successively rejected Japanese goods, deeply worried that Japan would rebel and treat the British Empire's dominions as it treated China. This is the second reason. On the contrary, the relationship between the United States and the British dominions is very close. Canada is the most powerful dominion, but its population is only one-tenth of the United States. Most of its domestic resources are exploited by American capital. The American Navy is equal to the British Navy, and Canada and the United States have a common interest. The naval power of the United States also extends to South Africa, Australia, and New Zealand. Therefore, how to establish friendly relations with the United States and use the maritime advantage of the United States to alleviate the weakness of the British Navy is the third thing that the dominion authorities are concerned about.

In summary, the attitude of the British dominions is to seek cooperation between Great Britain and the United States to prevent Japanese aggression and to replace military diplomacy and alliance diplomacy with joint diplomacy and collective peace. Specifically, in Europe, the dominions only hope that the League of Nations will be a moral cooperative organization and will not use force. In the Pacific, they hope that the Washington Treaty system will continue to be maintained so that the United States and Japan will not clash, that Great Britain and the United States will reconcile, that the security of the territories of all countries will be guaranteed, and that the defense burden in the Pacific will be reduced and armaments will be reduced to reduce the chances of war. Once war breaks out, the existence of the various dominions will suffer a fatal blow. Now that the British government and the dominion governments have the same attitude, it is inevitable that Great Britain's actions in the Far East will be based on Anglo-American cooperation and will be aimed at maintaining the peace system under the Washington Treaty. Thirteen years ago, there was a diplomatic victory for the dominions, and then the Washington Conference was convened. The impact of this British Empire diplomatic discussion on Far Eastern relations is self-evident.

U.S. Treasury Secretary's Speech: No Change in Silver Policy; Stabilizing Currency Should Not Be the Sole Responsibility of the United States; Prefer to Use Hard Currency to Pay Trade Deficits 15

(Washington) In his radio address tonight, Treasury Secretary Morgenthau did not indicate any change in the U.S. silver policy. Although Morgenthau did not make any specific announcement regarding the silver purchase plan, he did say that the United States "will strive to make silver more useful in the monetary system because silver is used as currency by a large part of the world's population." Most of the Treasury Secretary's speech discussed the possibility of international currency stability. On this point, he stated that the United States is not unwilling to cooperate in stabilizing international exchange rates, but it is very unwilling to make unnecessary sacrifices that would cause the United States to suffer great losses in the world market. In short, "The world should know that if all countries are prepared to stabilize their foreign exchange rates, the United States will not obstruct it. We have been in the position of onlookers. We did not initiate any currency wars, but the losses we have suffered are immeasurable. Therefore, others should not blame us for having to bear the responsibility of restoring order. All of our current actions must be based on the certainty that we will no longer lose the benefits we have already recovered. We are not unwilling to stabilize currencies, but if countries still cannot maintain order, we can avoid being harmed. We have already revalued our currency, and we can change it again in the future. There is no restriction," he said.

However, Morgenthau also strongly asserted that the current U.S. dollar is very stable because "the government's monetary policy has allowed us to escape from chaos and continue to move forward towards recovery." Morgenthau also said that if the United States wants to fix the dollar or devalue it again, it is free to do so. However, the United States is only concerned with protecting normal foreign trade and does not want to dominate the entire world market. Therefore, "We not only do not want to compete in devaluation, but our currency is very stable. If we continue on this path, the countries of the world may eventually achieve practical stability. It is not impossible." However, the so-called stability does not mean that the United States will declare that it will no longer change the gold content of the dollar. If it does, it will only trigger a new round of devaluation competition in other countries. Morgenthau continued that the United States will certainly do its best to restore world prosperity, but it is also unwilling to allow countries that manipulate currencies to harm the United States for their own benefit. "If we plan our future foreign trade, we must first decide whether we are willing to sell goods to customers who cannot pay for them. Of course, we can collect more IOUs, and there are many international bankers who are willing to handle such procedures. But at present, what we are collecting is a large amount of gold and silver in cash. In addition to paying for trade deficits, this cash is also used by other countries to escape to the United States to seek refuge under our stable currency. Economists have said that if we collect all the cash in the world, there will be no more international trade in the future. But in fact, although our gold reserves have reached a previous record, the world's gold production is also increasing rapidly. Some people oppose our gold and silver policy, calling it a cause of the large amounts of gold and silver in the world not being able to circulate. However, our monetary reserves have also been enriched as a result. Debts that are not paid on time cannot be used as a reserve for our currency. Therefore, these debts can also be called a congestion of currency. If we do not want to choose one of the two, the government is willing to choose to use gold and silver to pay for international differences," the Treasury Secretary said. The Treasury Secretary also criticized the policies of former President Hoover, saying that from July 1914 to the end of 1932, the United States had exported a huge amount of goods worth $47 billion, and that $19 billion of these goods had not been repaid. (National Telegram, 13th)

(New York) According to Wall Street observers, Treasury Secretary Morgenthau's speech on the dollar today was issued by the U.S. government to probe whether European countries have any intention of stabilizing exchange rates. The financial community was generally disappointed with the Treasury Secretary's speech. The Treasury Secretary not only failed to clarify the government's attitude towards silver, but also failed to clearly describe the national currency issue. Some financial experts believe that the Treasury Secretary's failure to set a new price for silver is very disappointing. Some people also said that setting a new price for silver is a matter for the President. Also, most economists do not believe that the United States can obtain large amounts of gold and silver from foreign countries under the current policy. It is believed that the continuous inflow of this hard currency into the United States is enough to cause financial turmoil in other countries, especially in China, Mexico, Peru, and other countries. At the same time, these hard currencies in the United States will also become unproductive. However, businessmen generally expressed joy that the government intends to cooperate with other countries to stabilize exchange rates because if the exchange rates of the dollar and other currencies can be stabilized, it can restore mutual trust in the international market. It is still difficult to judge what impact the Treasury Secretary's speech will have on the market. Silver speculators are generally disappointed with it. At the same time, after the dollar stabilizes, the price of gold will not rise again, so gold buyers are also mostly waiting and watching. (National Telegram, 14th)

(Washington) In Treasury Secretary Morgenthau's speech, the U.S. financial community recognized the honest nature of the statement that the United States is unwilling to unilaterally fix the price of the dollar, but also does not want to hinder the process of international currency stability, which was unexpected. Some observers believe that this statement is intended to put the issue of currency stability before Great Britain, because the so-called section that the United States cannot proceed alone in the aspect of stability is tantamount to inviting the United States to cooperate in the process. It is said that before making his speech, Mr. Morgenthau carefully considered the remarks he intended to make with President Roosevelt. Therefore, Mr. Morgenthau is believed to be speaking as the representative of the full authority of the government. Senator Wheeler criticized the government's new measures and those who advocated immediate stability and are now criticizing the Treasury Secretary's remarks. In other words, President Roosevelt has obviously changed his position. President Roosevelt had previously stated that he would not consider stability unless the price level of 1926 was reached. In January of this year, President Roosevelt's remarks in Congress still stated that the average price level at that time was only 74.8 percent of the 1926 level. Now that the Treasury Secretary has made this statement, it can be seen that the positions are inconsistent before and after. (Reuters Telegram, 3rd)

Basel The Bank for International Settlements today issued an annual report attacking the U.S. silver policy, stating briefly that this policy has caused silver-using countries to suffer damage and has destabilized international exchange rates. The report continued that if the international need for silver were as great as that for gold, it would not be necessary to resort to artificial actions. At the same time, there is no indication that this action by the United States will fundamentally change the international status of silver. (National Telegram, 14th)

Italy Bans Silver Exports 16

(Rome) The government today issued an order strictly prohibiting the export of silver, regardless of silver blocks, silver bars, or silver dollars. Travelers are only allowed to carry 50 lire of silver coins when leaving the country. The effect of this order by the government is to prevent the country's silver from being transported abroad due to the rise in silver prices abroad. People had expected the government to take this action beforehand. (National Telegram, 14th)

(Rome) Italy today officially banned the export of silver. It is reported that Italy needs a large amount of cash silver in order to transport it to its colonies in North Africa. Therefore, this ban was issued. (Reuters Telegram, 14th)

Successful Belgian Monetary Policy; Capital Flows Back; Prices Return to Stability 17

Brussels, Belgium Prime Minister Zeeland made a speech at a banquet for foreign journalists. This was the first speech after the new cabinet issued its political declaration. Zeeland briefly stated that the government is determined to reform domestic affairs, and the success or failure can be seen at the end of this year. So far, the government has achieved some results: (1) Japanese capital has flowed back into Belgium in large amounts, indicating the success of Belgium's monetary policy. (2) The position of banks has been greatly consolidated. (3) The government does not support but restricts the increase in interest rates. (4) The prices of various securities have continued to increase within a moderate limit. (5) After the surge in prices, they have now returned to stability. In addition, Zeeland also said that devaluing the currency was not only to rescue the banks, but also to prevent the banks from stopping payment of debts, so it was necessary. Other countries devalue their currencies to obtain commercial benefits, but Belgium is not one of them. As for the government's policy outline in the second stage, there are the following two points: to enable industries to absorb unemployed workers, and to reduce the financial and tax burden by reducing interest rates. (Havas Telegram, 13th)

British Parliament Questions Chinese Affairs; Eden Satisfied with Trademark Amendment Law; Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Loan Issue Under Negotiation; Proof that Imported Chinese Eggs Have No Germs Is Successful 18

(London) Today in the House of Commons, Conservative MP Crooke-Lawton asked the government to pay attention to the amendment of the Chinese Trademark Law and advocated negotiating with the Chinese government to provide better protection for British trademarks. Lord Privy Seal Eden replied that the revised text of the Chinese Trademark Law is obviously better than the original and that the current difficulties can be overcome. Conservative MP Mauren asked the government to pay attention to the unpaid Shanghai-Fengjing section of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway line loan. Eden replied that negotiations have been conducted many times without result. British Ambassador to China, Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen, is now working hard on this matter. Mauren also inquired about the detention of British national Parsons in Gansu Province. Eden replied that the officials accused Parsons of stealing antiquities from caves, so he was detained. The British Embassy in Peiping has negotiated with the Chinese government, and the Chinese Foreign Minister has agreed to send a telegram to the Gansu Provincial Governor to send Parsons to Peiping and provide protection along the way. Eden traveled to various European capitals last month due to diplomatic issues and was very tired, resulting in illness for a long time after returning to England. Today he attended the House of Commons, so when he stood up to answer the MPs' questions, everyone applauded to welcome him. (Reuters Telegram, 13th)

(London) Today the House of Commons again paid attention to Chinese chicken eggs and the food of Chinese chickens. Parliamentary Under-Secretary of State for Health, Shakespeare, replied to Conservative MP Hanlon's question, saying that he did not know whether he had studied the quality of Chinese chicken eggs in terms of food. What has been studied recently is the bacterial composition of Chinese chicken eggs. He heard that no spoilage occurred when chicken eggs were removed from freezing. Hanlon said that Chinese chicken eggs are produced under conditions that make people nauseous and should be immediately banned from import. Labour MP Lawson said that the standard of living of Chinese chickens is lower than that of British chickens. This remark caused loud laughter. Shakespeare replied that the content of eggs changes depending on the food of the chickens. It appears that the Ministry of Health has not yet received the resolution of the National Poultry Association's meeting on April 30 opposing the import of Chinese eggs. Shakespeare also reiterated the statement made by egg importers on March 13 that "no disease has ever been found to originate from chicken eggs from China" (Reuters Telegram, 13th)

New Constitution of the Philippines; Public Referendum Held; Ratio of Approval to Disapproval is Nine to One 19

(Manila) Judging from the voting situation in the 14 provinces that have been partially announced in the Philippine Constitution, which has been passed by the United States and approved by the U.S. President, the majority is in favor of this constitution. Votes in favor account for 91.773, while votes against account for only 11.475. Therefore, the previous panic in the United States over the Philippines has now disappeared. (National Telegram, 14th)

(Manila) A public referendum was held today to determine the number of people who approved of the new Philippine Constitution. The process was quite smooth, and no disturbances were reported. The results have not yet been announced. According to the initial report, the ratio of those in favor to those against is 50 to 1. It is generally believed that Philippine Senate President Quezon has a high chance of being elected as the first president of the Philippines. (Reuters Telegram, 14th)

Japanese Army Plans Second National Defense Plan; Total Expenditure of 600 Million Yuan to Be Completed Within Five Years; Expand the Strength of the Kwantung Army and Train for Mainland Operations 20

(Tokyo) According to Japanese military sources, the Japanese Army plans to carry out a second national defense plan starting next year. The specific plan is being drafted by the Military Affairs Bureau and will be submitted to the next Diet. The contents are as follows:

(1) The total expenditure is set at 600 million yuan. (2) It will be implemented in stages over a five-year plan. (3) The initial expenditure (1936) is set at 120 million yuan. (4) The goals of the new national defense plan: (A) To replenish new-style military equipment and ammunition, expand the organization and equipment of the various peacetime divisions. (B) To expand the mechanized corps and strengthen the combat effectiveness of the army. (C) To replenish the strength of the Kwantung Army, strengthen its connection with the mainland forces, and intensify training for mainland operations. (Hualian Telegram, 14th)

Franco-Soviet Conference to Expand the Peace Movement; Drafting a Non-Aggression Pact for Eastern Europe; Laval Meets with Soviet Officials 21

(Moscow) Litvinov and Laval met for an hour and a half, and the meeting was very pleasant. At the time, Secretary-General of the French Foreign Ministry, Alexis Léger, Soviet Ambassador to France, Valerian Dovgalevsky, French Ambassador to the Soviet Union, Charles Alphand, and Laval's Chief of Staff, René Ristelhueber, were present. (TASS Telegram, 14th)

(Moscow) French Foreign Minister Laval and Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov held their first meeting this afternoon, which lasted two hours. Both sides were reportedly quite satisfied with the progress of the meeting. Laval's visit is seen as clear evidence of France and Russia's willingness to guarantee European peace, which the Russian authorities are very pleased with. The Soviet Union is now willing to welcome Poland's cooperation, as Russia and Poland have already signed a non-aggression pact. The Soviet Union is now preparing to expand relations between the two countries on a broader basis. It is generally felt that the talks between the French and Russian diplomatic authorities may be the prelude to a broad peace movement, taking the form of expanding the general security pact and concluding an Eastern European pact. (Reuters Telegram, 13th)

(Moscow) At 3:30 this afternoon, French Foreign Minister Laval and Soviet People's Commissar for Foreign Affairs Litvinov held their first talks at the Commissariat for Foreign Affairs, which lasted for an hour. No communiqué was issued afterwards. According to our correspondent, Laval informed Litvinov of the results of his talks in Warsaw, and then discussed the ratification of the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact and reviewed the international situation. They also discussed the possibility of concluding a regional Eastern European pact when necessary, including the following points: (1) The signatory countries will not invade each other. (2) In the event of an invasion, they will consult each other and agree not to assist the aggressor country. Today, Laval visited Lenin's Mausoleum and is scheduled to meet with Soviet Communist Party General Secretary Stalin, Chairman of the Central Executive Committee Kalinin, and Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars Molotov tomorrow. Tonight, Foreign Commissar Litvinov hosted a banquet to welcome Laval. At the end of the banquet, Litvinov issued a statement saying that the establishment of the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact is sufficient to prove that both countries want to actively guarantee peace in substance. Any country that feels interested in maintaining peace can join this pact. Laval replied that France and Russia freely unite their forces not only for the sake of defending their own security, but also to serve the general peace. All governments and peoples must work together to achieve the cause of international collective ties. (Havas Telegram, 13th)

(Moscow) French Foreign Minister Laval met with Communist Party Secretary-General Stalin and Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars Molotov in the Kremlin this morning. At noon, he had a banquet with Molotov and other People's Commissars. (Reuters Telegram, 14th)

Litvinov Banquets Laval: Jointly Unveiling the Principles of the Accord, Emphasizing Cooperation Without Exclusion 22

(Moscow) Foreign Commissar Litvinov hosted a banquet on the 13th in honor of French Foreign Minister Laval, as well as Rosa Chat and Leger, who accompanied Laval to the Soviet Union. Soviet government members such as Voroshilov, Mezhlauk, Tsekoyan, Grinko, Bubnov, Krestinsky, Soviet Ambassador to France Potemkin, French Ambassador to the Soviet Union Alphand, personnel from the French Embassy, and senior officials from the Foreign Affairs Committee all attended the banquet. Litvinov and Laval exchanged speeches on the spot. After the banquet, a grand reception followed. Members of the diplomatic corps, government commissioners, senior officials from various People's Committees, representatives from Soviet public organizations, as well as figures from the scientific and artistic communities, and domestic and foreign journalists were all present. (TASS dispatch, 14th)

(Moscow) In his welcoming address to Laval, Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov stated, "We can resolutely declare that the convention we have concluded is an instrument of peace. The first distinctive feature of this agreement is the fervent desire of those who drafted it to prevent the emergence of any circumstances that could hinder its implementation. The agreement itself will serve as evidence of the firm determination of the two major European powers to safeguard peace through active and practical means, and this is precisely how the aforementioned objective will be achieved. The second characteristic of the agreement is that it not only does not target any country, but also does not reject any country that is willing to join and willing to fulfill the tasks of the agreement. As the convention is an instrument of peace, it will inevitably strengthen and solidify existing instruments of peace. I am referring to the Covenant of the League of Nations. The convention concluded this time is a necessary supplement to the Covenant. This agreement, with a few exceptions, has won the support and sympathy of various countries and all true friends of peace. I dare to hope that the signing of this agreement is not the culmination of Franco-Soviet cooperation, but the beginning of such cooperation, which is beneficial to all countries when they are engaged in peaceful development in an environment where peace has not been disrupted." (TASS dispatch, 14th)

(Moscow) In his reply to Litvinov, Laval first expressed gratitude for the warm reception. He then stated, "Your Excellency's expression of the Soviet government's policy reaffirms how deeply the Soviet people hope to participate in and bear the responsibility for building European security. We have created a tool for peace; this is the definition you have given, and it is the best definition of the Franco-Soviet pact. Our negotiations were indeed based on equal terms, and the conclusion of these negotiations is also based on equality. All rights and responsibilities on both sides are of an equivalent nature." Laval then expressed that peace is the most needed thing, so he hoped that other countries could also participate in this work of building peace. Laval added, "The realization of necessary amity among nations can be said to be a long and arduous task, so responsible political leaders must have patience and indomitable spirit. Both you and I possess this kind of spirit; this has been demonstrated by our actions. All countries have a collective obligation to international solidarity, because peace is indivisible. Therefore, we must engage in this, and from now on we will continue to appeal to the conscience of governments until this request is heard." (TASS dispatch, 14th)

Balkan Nations Endorse Franco-Russian Accord, Also Agreeing to Participate in the Danube River Convention 23

Bucharest: The Balkan Entente conference has concluded its current session. An official communique was issued, stating that the current state of the Balkan Peninsula is quite satisfactory. As for the Franco-Russian mutual assistance pact, it is the foundation for the future security system of Eastern Europe. The Balkan Entente countries all endorse it. The Entente countries are prepared to sign the Danube River Convention, but only on the condition that the legitimate interests of the relevant countries are respected. Regarding various economic issues, the Entente countries decided to promote mutual trade relations, expressed support for the draft convention on the development of air transport, and studied the establishment of a Balkan Peninsula Bank. France and Italy Sign Aviation Cooperation Agreement, Also Discussing the West European Sky Convention 24

(Rome) French Air Minister Denain and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini signed an aviation agreement here today, stipulating close cooperation between Italian and French commercial aviation. It is reported that the cooperation between the two countries is sufficient to promote the new Paris-Rome air route, as well as the opening of the Tunis-Tripoli connection line in African territories. The landing field of the Marseille-Saigon line operated by France will also be opened in Italian territory. In addition, both countries have made concessions to each other regarding the opening of the France-Turin-Milan-Venice and Turin-Lyon lines. (National Telegraph, 14th)

(Rome) French Air Minister General Tran held talks with Prime Minister Mussolini, and Air Undersecretary Valle was also present. A communique was issued afterwards, stating that what the Prime Minister and General Tran discussed was the realization of the West European Sky Mutual Assistance Convention advocated by the Anglo-French London Declaration and the Stresa Conference. Various conditions for technical cooperation between the Italian and French air forces and the measures they are willing to take when necessary will be decided. In addition, an agreement on civil aviation cooperation between Italy and France has been signed, the main points of which stipulate the establishment of air routes between Paris and Rome, and between French-owned Tunisia and Italian-owned Tripolitania in Africa. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

(Rome) Aviation technical cooperation between Italy and France has already begun, such as the exchange of information between the two countries on aircraft under construction, which is one aspect of cooperation. Today, technicians from both countries held consultations on this matter. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

(Rome) The aviation agreement between France and Italy stipulates that once the consent of the Egyptian government is obtained, an air route will be opened between French-owned Tunisia and Italian-owned Tripolitania in Africa. At present, the section from Marseille to Beirut, Syria, of the Marseille-Saigon air traffic operated by France uses seaplanes. After the establishment of the Franco-Italian agreement, French aircraft can fly over Italian airspace, so both land and sea aircraft can be used on this line. French Air Minister General Tran hosted a banquet last night for important Italian figures. Undersecretary of Foreign Affairs Suvich, Undersecretary of the Navy Admiral Gavaseni, Undersecretary of Aviation Valle, and French Ambassador Chamberlin were all present. Tran, on behalf of the French government, presented medals to Italian air force officers. (Havas dispatch, 14th)

Air Raid Drill in Paris 26

(Paris) Government agencies and residents of the entire city jointly held an air raid drill. The entire city was in turmoil, and sirens blared incessantly everywhere. Factory workers and people gathered in various places abandoned their daily work and put on gas masks, while other people rushed to bomb shelters and gas shelters. The streets were emptied, and transportation also ceased. (National Telegraph, 14th)

Italian-Abyssinian Border Dispute: Italy Willing to Resolve Through Arbitration, Note to Abyssinian Government, Large Numbers of Troops Continuously Sailing to East Africa 27

(Rome) The Italian government issued a note to the Abyssinian government today, expressing its willingness to submit the border dispute between the two countries to the Conciliation Committee in accordance with the 1928 Italian-Abyssinian treaty. The Italian government has selected the Italian representative to the committee. The Italian government's move today follows the Abyssinian government's application for immediate intervention by the League of Nations in the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. The Abyssinian government's recent document to the League of Nations mentioned (1) the Italian government has asked certain national governments to prohibit their nationals from being appointed as arbitrators in the dispute; (2) denying the Italian claim that Abyssinia has issued a general mobilization order; and (3) declaring that the Abyssinian government is willing to accept the judgment of a fair arbitration tribunal. The Italian note to Abyssinia was just published, and the Italian newspaper simultaneously carried an article criticizing the partiality of some British newspapers, saying that any European intervention may encourage Abyssinian hostility and cannot weaken Italy's military power to defend its national rights. Although Italy is using troops in East Africa, if the work of reconciliation and cooperation that Italy hopes for fails, Italy's position is still capable of coping with any events in Europe. The dispute between Italy and Abyssinia arose from armed Abyssinians occasionally invading the disputed area between Abyssinia and Italian Somaliland. In recent months, there have been several clashes between the two sides. Mussolini, in order to cope with possible events, has sent tens of thousands of troops to Eritrea and Italian Somaliland. (Reuters dispatch, 13th)

(Rome) The Italian government has recently dispatched a large number of troops to East Africa. The mail ship "Colombo" is scheduled to set sail on May 16, carrying 1,000 soldiers from the Gavina Division to East Africa. The mail ship "Venci" will also depart on the same day, carrying 1,200 artillery soldiers with cannons. The mail ship "Dalmasi" will carry 570 officers and soldiers, and the mail ship "Bolun Chai" will depart on May 17, carrying 200 soldiers and ammunition. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

(Geneva) The Abyssinian government has recently sent a note to the Secretariat of the League of Nations regarding the dispute between Italy and Abyssinia, stating that Italy has repeatedly mobilized and dispatched large armies to Italian-owned Eritrea and Somalia in East Africa. Therefore, Abyssinia requests the Council of the League of Nations to consider the situation created by Italy's actions, and states that the Abyssinian government has repeatedly requested the establishment of an arbitration committee in accordance with the 1928 Italian-Abyssinian treaty to resolve the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, but Italy has ignored it and tried to persuade foreign governments not to send representatives to participate when they receive requests to participate in the arbitration committee. For this reason, Abyssinia hopes that the Council will promptly take measures to resolve the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, so as to respect Abyssinia's territorial integrity and political independence. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

(Geneva) The Secretariat of the League of Nations received a new note from the Abyssinian government today, but its full text has not yet been published. According to well-informed sources, the Abyssinian government is applying for the League of Nations to pay attention to certain new military plans of the Italian side and the fact that the Italian-Abyssinian arbitration committee has not yet been organized. If the conciliation committee has not been organized before the League of Nations Council meeting on May 20, the Abyssinian government requests that the League of Nations Council handle the matter. The Secretariat of the League of Nations is now publishing the additional agenda for the next League of Nations Council meeting. The dispute between Hungary and Yugoslavia is also included in the agenda. It is widely rumored here that the South Hungarian dispute can be resolved without causing major difficulties. The foreign ministers of the Little Entente countries will all go to Geneva to take the opportunity to hold preliminary talks on the Danube River conference. In addition, there are several issues related to the Free City of Danzig. (National Telegraph, 13th)

(Geneva) According to information obtained here, the situation of the dispute between Italy and Abyssinia is very difficult. Recently, British Ambassador to France Sir Clerk received instructions from the government to consult with the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs, so that Britain and France could jointly find a way to urge the establishment of the Italian-Abyssinian mixed arbitration committee. However, what kind of attitude Britain and France will take will depend on the outcome of the consultation. Now, the Abyssinian government has sent another note to the League of Nations Council, requesting it to handle it quickly in order to resolve the dispute between the two countries. In short, the situation of this dispute is very tricky. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

Polish Government Decides on Piłsudski's State Funeral, Various Countries Send Telegrams of Condolences 28

Warsaw: Marshal Piłsudski's body will be moved from the Belvedere Palace to the Cathedral on Thursday evening, where it will remain for thirty-six hours, so that the people of the capital can pay their respects to the Marshal's remains. As for when it will be transported from here to Krakow for burial, it may not be decided until Thursday evening, but the special train carrying the Marshal's body will definitely stop for a moment in the places it passes, so that the people can pay their respects. (National Telegraph, 14th)

Warsaw: The Polish President has appointed former Undersecretary of the Army General Gaspard Spierski to succeed General Piłsudski as Chief of the Army, and General Smilley to succeed as Inspector General of the Polish Army. The new Chief of the Army issued an order to the Polish army today, urging them to be loyal to the country, and ordered the entire army to read the President's proclamation. All troops will wear mourning attire, and officers of all ranks will wear black gauze. The Cabinet met today, chaired by Prime Minister Stavik, and decided on a state funeral for Piłsudski, and ordered theaters and other entertainment venues to close on that day. All military personnel will wear black gauze for six weeks. There will be no wreaths in front of Piłsudski's coffin. Government officials have donated 5,500 Zloty to build Piłsudski's tombstone in Krakow. (National Telegraph, 14th)

Warsaw: The tense emotions caused by the death of General Piłsudski have now eased somewhat. The government and the people are now preparing for the memorial proceedings in the coming days. All public and private houses are flying at half-mast, and theaters and cinemas are closed. Radio stations only broadcast funeral music and news about Piłsudski's death in the capital. Piłsudski's remains are displayed in the Belvedere Palace, and four generals stand guard in front of the palace. Mrs. Piłsudski and her two daughters are also by his side. Citizens from cities and villages are vying to go to church to pray for the deceased and the future of the country. Catholic churches are holding special services, and most of the participants are villagers. The simplicity of the villagers makes the solemnity of the worship ceremony even more apparent. Krakow is Piłsudski's birthplace, and his remains will be buried in the royal mausoleum there. However, Piłsudski's heart will be buried with his mother. Although the whole country is filled with grief, it is enough to show the strength of Poland, which is enough to overcome any national crisis. (National Telegraph, 14th)

Warsaw: The date for the funeral of the late Minister of Military Affairs General Piłsudski has not yet been decided, but it is likely to be on Saturday this week. The location will be Krakow, where the burial will take place. The Marshal's remains have now been placed in the coffin, and the lid of the coffin is made of crystal. It is scheduled to be moved to St. John's Cathedral tomorrow for public viewing. In general, the Marshal's remains will be carried by veterans of the European War from Kielce to Krakow, a distance of about 150 kilometers, which is expected to take three days. According to reports, in 1916, Piłsudski led Polish volunteers from Krakow to defeat the Russian army and capture Kielce. This time, he is following the opposite path to commemorate the Marshal's great achievements twenty years ago. The Cabinet ordered the entire country to observe mourning for six weeks. Before the funeral, all concerts and theaters will stop performing. It is rumored that German leader Hitler may come to pay his condolences in person. This news is not credible. The Italian government has decided to send its ambassador to Poland to represent the binding, and the Italian army will also send a special delegation to Poland. The French government will send Foreign Minister Laval and former Army Chief General Pétain to represent them at the funeral. Laval will stop briefly in Warsaw on his way back from Moscow. (Havas dispatch, 12th)

(Rome) After hearing the news of Marshal Piłsudski's death, Prime Minister Mussolini immediately sent a telegram to the Polish government, saying, "Shocked to hear of Marshal Piłsudski's passing, I would like to express my deepest condolences on behalf of the Fascist government and the Italian people. He was an example for soldiers and civilians, and his famous name will be immortal. All those who know and admire Piłsudski's great achievements cannot help but remember him." (National Telegraph, 13th)

(Berlin) Secretary General of the Prime Minister's Office Meisner visited Polish Ambassador Lipski today to convey Chancellor Hitler's condolences on the death of General Piłsudski. (National Telegraph, 13th)

(Moscow) After arriving in Moscow, French Foreign Minister Laval heard the news of General Piłsudski's death and immediately sent a telegram to Polish Foreign Minister Beck to express his condolences. (National Telegraph, 14th)

Five Organizations Form Committee to Test Cottonseed Gasoline Extraction 30

(Nanjing) Domestic highways are becoming increasingly developed, and gasoline leakage costs millions each year. After consulting with the Ministry of Industry, it is hoped to remedy this by extracting gasoline from plants. After research by the Industrial Experiment Institute and the School of Science of National Central University, it is believed that it is possible to extract gasoline from cottonseed. Representatives from five organizations, including the Economic Commission, the Transportation Committee of Five Provinces and Cities, the Industrial Experiment Institute, National Central University, and Jiangnan Automobile Company, have formed a Committee to Test Cottonseed Gasoline Extraction. The establishment meeting has been held. The Economic Commission and the Transportation Committee of Five Provinces and Cities will be responsible for funding and experimental materials, the Industrial Experiment Institute and National Central University will be responsible for technical engineering, and Jiangnan Automobile Company will use its automobiles for on-site application experiments. The composition and cost-effectiveness will not be known until the results of the experiment are available. (Special dispatch, 14th)

Northwest Scientific Expedition Team: Procedures for Transporting Specimens and Rocks to Europe 31

(Nanjing) The Northwest Scientific Expedition Team has 38 boxes of animal specimens and rocks to be transported to Sweden. The leader of the team, Sven Hedin, asked the Antiquities Preservation Committee to request the Ministry of Finance to instruct the Tianjin Customs to release them. The Ministry of Finance replied that items that are not within the scope of antiquities will be taxed and released; items that are within the scope of antiquities, since the team is responsible for returning them by a designated date, can be temporarily exempted from tax. If they are not returned by the deadline, the team leader and others will be responsible for returning the original items and should also pay export tax. This regulation should be specified in the contract before being complied with. (Special dispatch, 14th)

Yellow River Disaster Lottery to Continue for Another Year 34

(Nanjing) The Hebei Fellow-Provincials Association in Beijing, in view of the fact that counties such as Changpu and Dong in Hebei have suffered from Yellow River disasters for many years, with the number of affected people reaching hundreds of thousands, and the financial resources of Hebei Province are extremely tight and unable to provide relief, the disaster victims have relied entirely on the surplus profits of the Yellow River Disaster Lottery in recent years. Although the breach in Changyuan has been closed, the post-disaster reconstruction in the disaster area still needs to be carried out. The issuance period of the Yellow River Disaster Lottery will expire in May of this year, which is causing considerable panic among the disaster victims in southern Hebei. A representative has been sent to Beijing to appeal, earnestly requesting that it be continued for another year in order to continue to provide relief and carry out post-disaster reconstruction. Commercial and Maritime Disputes: Regulations for Both Handling Committees Completed 35

After they are promulgated and implemented in the future, the existing regulations for the Commercial Arbitration Office and the Civil Arbitration Regulations will be abolished. The temporary regulations for the Maritime Dispute Handling Committee are based on the Maritime Law and do not apply the commercial provisions, in order to ensure that they are independent and not affected by each other. Tan Zhen Discusses the Notary System 41

(Nanjing) The Judicial Yuan's meeting passed the implementation of the notary system and is currently drafting notary regulations. According to Tan Zhen, the Vice President of the Yuan, the notary system has long been implemented in various countries, but our country has not yet implemented it. Considering the current situation in our country, with so many lawyers and accountants, establishing separate notary personnel might create more disadvantages than advantages. Therefore, it is proposed to implement the notary system without establishing notary personnel. In the future, after implementation, the Ministry of Justice will designate a judge from each level of court to act as a notary, assisted by a clerk. This will achieve the practical benefits of notarization and avoid abuses. The notary regulations are expected to be submitted for discussion at the Judicial Yuan's meeting this month. However, this system is still a pioneering effort in our country, and it is planned to designate several provinces for pilot implementation first. (14th Dispatch)

Xu Tingyao Speaks in Kaifeng 53

(Kaifeng) On the morning of the 13th, people from all walks of life in Kaifeng held an enlarged memorial week at the auditorium of Henan University. More than 3,000 people attended, including Chairman Liu, key figures from the Party, government, and military, staff from various organizations and groups, and students from various schools. Xu Tingyao was invited to speak about his impressions of various countries. After an introduction by Chairman Liu, Xu spoke on the two aspects of personnel preparation and material preparation in various countries. Regarding personnel preparation, he discussed the implementation of a conscription system, requiring all young people to serve in the military, as in various European countries such as France, Germany, Italy, Russia, Czechoslovakia, and Turkey. He particularly emphasized the efforts of the German government and people to restore their inherent military strength and abolish treaties. The living standards in Europe are higher than those in the Far East, and their enjoyment of life is beyond what the people of East Asia can compare to. They not only do not consider military service a hardship but rather enjoy it. Regarding material preparation, he estimated that all military expenses in Germany amounted to approximately 1.5 billion gold marks, and other countries were not much different. Currently, governments of various countries are compiling statistics on the number of factories nationwide, calculating daily raw materials and products separately, and implementing centralized control. Finally, he reported on the social conditions of various countries and the significance of our country maintaining its inherent culture. (14th Central News Agency Dispatch)

The project is estimated to require one million yuan, with the Economic Commission allocating 540,000 yuan and the three provinces allocating 460,000 yuan. The Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission is responsible for supervision, with a deadline for completion by the end of June. The inspection is scheduled to be completed within one week. The Zhao Jinduo Murder Case in Jinan: Zhao Accuses His Sister of Incest in Court; Sister Willing to Disembowel Herself to Prove Her Virginity 58

(Jinan) Zhao Jinduo, a resident of Liujiazhuang in the southern suburbs of Jinan, surrendered himself after killing his brother, Jinduo, and was sentenced to life imprisonment. His mother and sister, Jinlan, appealed on his behalf. Unexpectedly, Zhao, influenced by his wife's words, stated in court that he killed his brother because he had committed incest with his sister, Jinlan. Jinlan, a graduate of a women's normal school, values her reputation as her life. She has decided to request the court to conduct a blood test on the 15th to determine if she is a virgin. If this still cannot prove her virginity, she is willing to disembowel herself in court. She is determined to end her life as long as she can prove that she is still a virgin. This case has attracted the attention of the entire city. (14th Dispatch)

High in the Alps, a St. Bernard Saves a Life and Receives a Medal 59

(Paris) "Baiti," a female St. Bernard dog raised by the troops stationed in the Alps, recently received a silver medal and an honorary collar for saving the life of a university student named Luedel. The incident is remarkable and worth recording. On March 9th of this year, Luedel and his friend were climbing the Alps when they reached the Galibier peak. Luedel lost his footing, was injured, and could not walk. Despite assistance, he could not move. His companion, in desperation, temporarily placed Luedel in a deep pit and went down the mountain for help. By the time the rescuers arrived, they could not find where Luedel was hidden. Fortunately, "Baiti" climbed the mountains and crossed the streams, and finally found him. It jumped into the pit and pressed its body against Luedel to keep him warm. This continued throughout the night, and Luedel was finally rescued the next day. The "Animal Compassion" Association heard of this act of righteousness and awarded it a silver medal and a collar to recognize its merit. General Dauss, commander of the defense force, personally presented the award. (13th Havas Dispatch)

International Commercial News - Reuters Special Commercial Report, May 14 71

Gold and Silver:

English Gold: London gold prices rose slightly today to 142 shillings and 8.5 pence, an increase of 2 pence.

English Silver: London silver market soared today. The spot price is 34.75 pence, up 1.25 pence. The futures price is 34.9375 pence, up 1.3125 pence. India and China were buying, and sellers were scarce. Market sentiment was uncertain at the close.

American Silver: The Mount Li silver market opened today, approximately 180 pounds higher, expressing sympathy for London prices. It is reported that Italy has banned silver exports.

Exchange Rates:

English-American: The London foreign exchange market opened today, and the pound sterling fell slightly due to purchases in continental Europe. Prices then trended upward. The English-American exchange rate opened at 4 US dollars, 87.75 cents, the same as the US-British closing price yesterday. It initially fell, then rose. After the first hour, the price was 4 US dollars, 87.5615 cents, 3.125 cents higher than the opening price. It continued to rise 3.75 cents at noon. The trend was relatively stable after that. It fell 1.25 cents at 1 PM, but rose 1.25 cents again at 2 PM to 4 US dollars, 87.9375 cents.

English-French: The opening price was 73.90 francs, down 10 pounds. There was a gradual upward trend in the morning. At 2 PM, the price was 74.04 francs, 14 pounds higher than the opening price.

Cotton and Wheat:

American Cotton: The New York cotton market was calm today, but prices were slightly higher than yesterday's close. There are rumors that the US Cotton Public Storage Agency wants to enter more futures, but the director of the agency predicts that government inventories will decrease by 1 million bales at the end of this cotton season.

English Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market continued to fall today, expressing sympathy for the American market. At 1 PM, the July futures price was 5 shillings and 5 pence, 25 cents lower than yesterday.

English Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market saw a slight increase in American cotton futures today. At 1 PM, the July futures price was 6.48, up 2 pounds.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened slightly higher this morning, with a continuing upward trend. Although there were reports of continued rain, the reduction in wheat supply caused the wheat price to rise.

Rubber:

New York: The New York rubber market opened approximately 15 pounds higher today. The end of the auto industry labor strike made the market cheerful. Furthermore, the export tax on rubber produced by the Dutch East Indies has recently been increased, which is also a reason for the improved market sentiment.

London: The London rubber market was stable today. At noon, the July and September futures were 5 pence and 9375, up 0.0625.

Securities:

New York: At the beginning of trading this morning in New York, the prices of most stocks were up except for a few. The bill approved by the Senate Interstate Commerce Committee to regulate or dissolve public utility and commercial banking companies still has many points of opposition, so public utility stocks were negatively affected. Railroad stocks also eased slightly. Among the stocks that rose in price, silver mining stocks rose the most. Auto stocks also rose because the auto industry labor strike has been resolved. Treasury Secretary Morgenthau's speech last night did not have a major impact. The prices are as follows:

Wang Kemin and Huang Fu Report on the Political Situation in North China; Huang Could Go to Nanjing Within Days to Assume the Concurrent Post of Minister of Interior 79

Hangzhou Correspondence: Wang Kemin, member of the Executive Yuan's Beiping Political Reorganization Committee and Chief Advisor, is reporting to Committee Chairman Huang Fu on matters awaiting decision from the Beiping Political Reorganization Committee and seeking instructions on all matters. He and his wife and staff specially traveled south from Beiping to visit Huang at Moganshan. At 7:32 PM on the afternoon of the 12th, Wang Kemin, his wife and staff, and Wu Zhenxiu, the president of the Bank of China in Nanjing, and his wife arrived in Hangzhou on the Shanghai-Nanjing express train. Jin Runquan, the president of the Bank of China in Hangzhou, also happened to be returning to Hangzhou on the same train. He immediately sent cars to greet Wang and others to rest at the Die Lai Hotel on West Lake. At 8:30 AM on the 13th, Wang and Wu Zhenxiu and others traveled by car prepared by the Bank of China to Moganshan, arriving at Yucun Station at about 10 AM. They changed to sedan chairs to visit Huang Fu at his private residence at No. 509 to report everything and seek instructions. They attended a banquet hosted by Huang at his residence at noon. They left the mountain at 5 PM and returned to Hangzhou. At 7 PM, Jin Runquan specially hosted a banquet for Wang and Wu at the Laiyin Villa on West Lake. Huang Shaohong, Chairman of the Provincial Government, Xu Qingfu, Director of the Department of Finance, Zhou Xiangxian, the Mayor of Hangzhou, and Jiang Menglin, President of Peking University, who had arrived in Hangzhou the previous day, were invited to accompany them. The banquet lasted until 10:30 PM. Wang Shulu, Wu Zhenxiu, and their families took the Shanghai-Hangzhou early express train to Shanghai at 8:15 AM this (14th) morning. The reporter specially interviewed Wang at the station. According to Wang, this trip to Moganshan to visit Committee Chairman Huang was to report on the affairs of the Beiping Political Reorganization Committee and to seek instructions. Huang's arm and nose ailments have largely healed, and he could descend the mountain and go to Nanjing within the week to assume the concurrent post of Minister of Interior, but the date has not yet been determined. The situation in North China is currently very stable. The rotation of the war zone security teams is progressing smoothly and could be completed within two weeks. Regarding the Japanese ban on Chinese laborers leaving the customs, tens of thousands of Chinese laborers who had been lingering at various passes along the Great Wall have now completely left the customs. Other Chinese laborers within the customs are still continuing to enlist and leave the customs. The financial situation in North China is still good. Expenses are 80,000 yuan per month, which are allocated by the Central Government. The local income of Hebei Province is 20 million yuan per year. Income and expenditures are equal, and there is no deficit. After the Beiping Political Reorganization Committee abolished the agricultural administration group, it established a rural cooperative committee to handle rural loans at an interest rate of 4% to 6%. More than 2 million yuan were loaned out last year. Because the credit of the farmers is extremely good, more than 90% of the loans were recovered at maturity. The results exceeded expectations. Loans are still being made this year to benefit spring plowing. I will stay in Shanghai for about a week and then return north. I may need to visit President Wang in Nanjing to report everything.

Zhang Dingcheng's Remnant Bandits Fleeing to the Guangdong Border Surrounded; Deng's Division Convenes Security Meeting 80

Shantou News: The remnant bandits of Zhang Dingcheng's group in western Fujian were defeated by the National Army and fled into the mountains bordering Dabu and Raoping in Guangdong, causing great disturbance in Hecun, Dachan, Shangxiashan, and other places. The 80th Division of the National Army has already advanced into Pinghe. After recovering the bandit nest in Xianghu Mountain last month, they immediately telegraphed the Guangdong side to send troops to block them. Huang Renhuan then ordered Zeng Youren, the commander of the 1st Brigade, to move from Jiaoling to Huliao in Dabu, to supervise Chen Shaowu's troops stationed in Dabu and Ye Weihao's regiment stationed in Raoping to jointly suppress the bandits. Because of the lack of ammunition and food, Zhang's bandits looted in Shangxiashan and Xiuzhuan in Zhao'an, but were repelled by the militia. On the 3rd of this month, they fled back to Xiyanshan on the border of Raoping and Dabu. On the 4th, the garrison troops of Pinghe, Dabu, and Raoping divided their forces into three routes to suppress them. Kong, the commander of the Raoping battalion, occupied Lingtou, and the bandits retreated towards Jiuzizhang. At that time, the National Army had already advanced from Xiuzhuan in Zhao'an to the front of Shangrao Temple. The Dabu defense forces also mobilized from Shiyun towards Gangtou on the afternoon of the 4th to intercept the Zhang bandits' escape route. From the evening of the 4th, fierce fighting broke out between the two sides in the mountains. It is reported that Zhang's bandits have been surrounded, and a part of them scattered and fled downstream along the Han River. Deng Longguang's division also advanced to suppress the remnant bandits in Nanshan. On the 4th and 5th, they convened security meetings in Huilai and Puning and repaired power lines. It is reported that the Guangdong military ordered the two division commanders Huang and Deng to clear the remnant bandits on the Fujian-Guangdong border and in the Chaozhou area by the end of this month. (8th)

Chen Mingge Discusses Improving Jinpu Railway Operations; Through Train Service Between Banpei Will Shorten Travel Time by Four Hours; More Than 300 Freight Cars, Coal Cars, and Locomotives Purchased 81

Beijing News: Chen Mingge, the acting chairman of the Jinpu Railway, recently inspected the entire line with committee member Qian Zongyuan, secretary Ye Shumiao, chief of the engineering department Wu Yiming, chief of the police department Gao Li'an, and others, to lay the groundwork for improving railway operations. This inspection was relatively thorough, lasting half a month for the round trip. Chen has already returned to Beijing after completing his official duties. According to Chen, his impressions from this trip and the main points of the railway administration reform plan for the 24th year are as follows:

Past Overview: Chen first stated that Mr. Qiu Gongjing, the former chairman of the railway, had been in office for three years. Considering the deep-rooted problems of the railway in the past, he was determined to focus on fundamental work, such as repairing bridges, replacing sleepers, and improving the work efficiency of employees, achieving great results. Since he took over as acting chairman, the fundamental work has been largely completed. The second step of the plan is to promote business, hoping that business will develop day by day. When Chairman Qiu passed away, the employees of the railway still worked hard and did not show any signs of laziness or unease. This point can be proved by comparing the business performance in March and April of last year with the same months this year. The business revenue in March last year was 1.8 million, and in April it was 1.78 million. The revenue in March this year was 2.12 million, and in April it was 1.8 million, with a total increase of more than 300,000.

Reform Plan: As for the plan to improve railway operations, it is roughly divided into three points and will be implemented starting from the 24th year. (1) Through train service between Banpei: The original travel time was 28 hours each time. Now, for the convenience of passenger and freight transport, it has been decided to shorten the time. On the 5th of this month, the transportation department conducted a trial run. Departing from Pukou, it took a little over 24 hours to reach Beijing, which is 4 hours less than the original time. After implementation in the future, not only will passengers have increased convenience, but the railway will also benefit greatly from the allocation of vehicles. This matter can be implemented after the Ministry of Railways convenes a joint transportation meeting on the 16th of this month. (2) Because the business of the railway has been progressing in recent years, the original passenger and freight vehicles and locomotives are not sufficient for allocation. Now, 300 new-style freight and coal cars have been purchased. Among them, some coal cars have the latest structure. Just by loosening the screws at the bottom of the car, the entire carload of coal can be unloaded in an instant. There are also 16 Emperor locomotives, which can also be shipped in November. (3) After the number of vehicles has been increased, the repair work will inevitably become more important. The railway's original machine repair factories in Peikou, Jinan, and Tianjin will be improved at the same time. The steps are divided into two aspects: (A) In terms of manpower, increase work efficiency. Currently, the workers in the three factories do not stop working even on Sundays, but they still need to intensify their work in the future. (B) Add more machines and boilers to make the equipment more abundant.

Inspection Impressions: I inspected all the important locations along the entire line, such as Xuzhou, Yanzhou, and Jinan, in detail. I am quite satisfied with the general situation. Since the promotion of the New Life Movement, the service spirit of the employees has been particularly evident. Regarding the troops stationed along the way, they all maintain strength. The purpose of our trip is to increase the efficiency of transportation to facilitate merchants and travelers. The above are all facts. There are many other plans that are still in the planning stage and I do not want to report them in advance to avoid the drawbacks of empty talk. (Daily News)

Rich Mineral Resources in Southern Anhui; Gold Mines Discovered in Jixi Lianchuan Ridge 82

Wuhu News: Huizhou [southern Anhui] has steep mountains, so it has extremely rich deposits, and the mineral veins are so abundant that they are almost everywhere. Several years ago, scholars in Jixi engaged in panning for gold sand, but ultimately it was difficult to attract attention due to inconvenient transportation. Abandoning the goods on the ground is quite regrettable. Since the completion of the Hangzhou-Huizhou-Wuhu-Tunxi highways, the name of Huangshan has been widely known for a time, and the number of travelers has also increased daily. As a result, many mineral products in the Huizhou mountains have gradually become known. The product exhibition along the Wuhu-Tunxi Road, which is currently being held, has collected various minerals and displayed them separately, which further proves the abundance of mineral resources. Except for the hematite mine in Yangjiawu, Jingzhou, which has recently been officially mined, the copper and crystal mines were both accidentally discovered. The copper mine is located in Anzhuwu Yinshan on the border of Jixi and Ningguo. Because nearby residents picked up mountain rocks and put them in a furnace, they found green light flashing and a crackling sound. It was once rumored as a strange story. After Jianhua verified it, it was confirmed to be a copper mine. Gold mines have appeared in Dalijiao Lianchuan Ridge in Jixi and have been widely rumored for a long time. There is a lot of gold sand mixed in the river gravel in that area. People mostly pan for gold with gold boats (a tool made for panning gold that looks like a boat). The method is quite clumsy, so the amount of gold obtained is also uncertain. Gold sand must be dug three feet deep in the pond to obtain it, but you must be familiar with water to be able to retrieve it. Those with skillful techniques and good luck can get a profit of two or three yuan a day, otherwise, they only get one or two jiao a day. Last year, Wang Fuquan, a professor at Fudan University in Shanghai, and Gui Bujun, a technician from the Ministry of Industry, went to investigate and dug up mineral samples, which they took back for verification. Recently, Jiang Shaojie, a mine merchant, presented it to the Anhui Construction Department, and the department dispatched technician Shen Guozhen to conduct a joint survey, intending to raise funds to mine silver mines in Xiawu, also on the border of Xuancheng and Ningguo. There is a huge cave with a diameter of 189 meters on the mountainside in that area. The geology is brightly pure white. After a little refining, it becomes pure silver. In the 16th year of the Republic [1927], a Mr. Chen dug up a sample and spent more than a thousand yuan to have it tested in Tunxi. He then felt that the transportation was inconvenient and the costs were too high, so he stopped. The current authorities are considering how to deal with this matter. (13th)

Current Traffic Situation Between Xi'an and Lanzhou; Fast and Comfortable, Far From What It Used To Be 83

Since the Longhai Railway trains reached Xi'an, the people of the country have been paying attention to the development of the Northwest. Some go to engage in business, and some organize groups to go for investigation. The news in the newspapers is endless. This kind of meaningful action is truly a great phenomenon in recent years. However, the Northwest has a vast scope, and Lanzhou in Gansu Province should be the key point. This is the destination of the general investigators of the Northwest, and it is also a necessary route. However, Lanzhou is far to the northwest of Xi'an, more than 1,400 li away from Xi'an. This kind of long journey inevitably makes those who enjoy comfort retreat. Here is a general description of the travel situation from Xi'an to Lanzhou for reference. The Longhai Railway has special express trains running east and west every day. The first and second class sleeper dining cars and food can satisfy the passengers in every way, so there is no need to go into details. When you arrive in Xi'an, the new-style hotels in the area have already opened, and there is also a feeling of being at home. Xi'an is the capital of Shaanxi Province, and the people and customs already have the Northwest situation. Moreover, the railway has just opened, and the local area is working hard on construction, and it is also an important emerging market. Those who want to promote domestic goods see this as a newly developed route for commerce. In the city of Chang'an, there are many things to see and do. Those who want to travel to famous places and enjoy the scenery, such as the majestic Mount Hua in the west and the beautiful hot springs of Huaqing Pool, are all near the Longhai Road and are also enough for elegant scholars to appreciate. Departing from Xi'an, there is the Xi'an-Lanzhou Highway operated by the Economic Commission, which has been open to traffic since May 1st of this year. It runs between Xi'an and Lanzhou once a day, and it takes four days to reach Lanzhou from Xi'an. The speed is still not slow. Compared with the previous camel and mule carts, the speed is ten times faster. Moreover, the road is equipped with ten newly purchased large-sized long-distance buses for passengers, each car can accommodate 30 passengers, the seats are comfortable, and the interior of the car is spacious. There are a total of twelve stations on the route, and the major stations are equipped with hotels and cafeterias. With the efforts of the Shaanxi and Gansu authorities along the way, the area is very peaceful. After this, the convenience for people traveling to and from the Northwest can be generally seen.
