It is now known that the order of the provincial hall has been received, dismissing inspector Tao Shixiu as a warning.

Taicang; A Tragic Incident Amidst the Welcoming Gods Festival 86

In this county's cities and villages, it is customary to welcome gods and hold festivals at the end of spring and the beginning of summer. Generally, idlers and ignorant villagers flock to them. Each temple takes turns to perform and compete for many days, wasting people and money. The authorities have never prohibited them. Today (the 13th) is the main day of Cao'an outside Chaoyangmen. All the temples in the southeast township must participate as an example. At noon, the parade starts at Ban Jingwan outside Chaoyangmen. The number of spectators is overwhelming. Anyone who wants to go from Henan to Hebei to watch must cross the Liu River, so temporary ferries are prepared to transport the spectators back and forth. After lunch, the ferry went north from the south bank, because it was overloaded, the boatman could not stop it. The boat was small and there were too many people, and the movements were inconsistent. In a moment, it sank, and more than thirty people on the boat were drowned. They tried their best to rescue them, but because the river was deep and the water was rapid, five people were unaccounted for. It was not until dusk that one person was rescued, but he had been dead for a long time, and there was no way to revive him. As of the time the reporter sent the manuscript, the other four people had not yet been rescued.

Kunshan; County Chief Peng Sued 87

Wang Pijia, a local resident, was wanted by the county government last year for a case and has not yet been apprehended. It is now known that Wang sued County Chief Peng Baichuan for abusing his power and filed a complaint with the High Court. After the High Court approved the lawsuit, it scheduled a hearing for the 15th. Now County Chief Peng has received a subpoena and has gone to Suzhou to await questioning.

Change of Head in the Experimental District 88

Zhu Wenyuan, the head of the county's autonomous experimental district, is doing business in Shanghai and has found it difficult to take care of district affairs. He has repeatedly resigned to the county government, but has not been approved. Now County Chief Peng has approved Zhu's firm intention to resign and has submitted a request to the provincial hall to appoint Xu Mingzhi, the head of the Xu Gongqiao Folk Education Center, to succeed him. It is reported that Xu went to take over the post immediately after being appointed.

Wuxi; Pottery Village Robbery Case Cracked 89

At 12 o'clock the night before last, six or seven bandits broke into the Muguang Nunnery in Taoji Village, the second district, and robbed it. They first tied up Wang Fujin, who was watching the nunnery, threatened him with guns, and forced him to reveal the location of the silver. Then they opened the room of Pei Dayou, the principal of the Muguang Elementary School, and wantonly searched and robbed, losing more than one hundred yuan. Afterwards, Xu Junde, a policeman from the fourth post of the first direct detachment of Dongmen, found Chen Pengfu (also known as Binghua, 22 years old, from Changshu), a bandit in this case, near Tingzi Bridge. A lot of the original loot was found. Zhang Fusheng and Gu Hui, the landlord, two suspects were also arrested at Nanmen. Yesterday, they were all taken to the Public Security Bureau to await interrogation.

Wonton Shop Owner Commits Suicide After Lost Love 90

Zhang Rensheng, a resident of Xiao Zhang Lane in the fourth district (Kaiyuan Township), was 36 years old. He used to work in Yan Ji wonton shop outside Jixiang Bridge in Guangfu. In August last year, he became intimate with a southern woman surnamed Li. They lived together like husband and wife. In February this year, he was fired for something. Recently, Rensheng opened a Heji wonton shop next to the Fuchang Hotel in Xinmin Bridge. The concubine Li also lived in the shop. A few days ago, Li's husband found out that his wife was intimate with Rensheng, so he came to the city alone, slapped Rensheng a few times, talked about the conditions, and took Li back to his hometown. Rensheng suffered this setback, losing both money and people. He was angry and annoyed, and had the idea of ​​being tired of the world. So he committed suicide by taking poison the night before last. The landlord noticed it and sent him to the nursing hospital for treatment. Because the poisoning was too deep, he died immediately. It was also tragic.

Jiading; Shanghai-Taicang Bus Accident Injures People 91

At 10 am on the 12th, the second Shanghai-Taicang bus arrived at the east gate of this county. Approaching the station, the driver, Zhang Zhaofu, had already turned off the air valve. When he arrived at the station, he turned on the brakes. Unexpectedly, the brakes suddenly broke down and continued to move forward. The road to the station was already at the end. If he continued forward, he would fall into the low-lying farmland, which would be dangerous. The driver turned the steering wheel sharply to the south because there were many passengers. The south was the road from the station to the city street. There were many rickshaws parked on both sides. There were wooden posts in the road to separate the station. Many rickshaw pullers were waiting for passengers outside the posts, which was quite crowded. When the bus rushed out of the wooden stake boundary to the south, the driver waved his hands repeatedly, but the rickshaw pullers were caught off guard and could not escape in time. Three people were hit by the car. Two people were only slightly injured. Among them, Shi Qianlang, a native of Chongming, who lived in Lou Tangzhen, had a large hole in his thigh crushed by the wheel, and his leg bone was broken. He fainted immediately. Stationmaster Lu Xizeng quickly helped him onto the bus and personally sent him to the Shanghai Shijiang Hospital for treatment.

Hangzhou; Four Suicide Cases Recorded Together 92

Suicide cases in Hangzhou have been emerging in an endless stream these days. They are recorded separately below. (1) Zhang Shoufa, a guest at Dafang Inn on Dongjie Road, committed suicide by hanging himself after losing his job and suffering from an incurable disease. The court verified the case and coffined it. (2) Zhou Pingzhang, a Taoist priest from Dongyue Temple in Liangzhu Town, Hang County, fell in love with Liang Jubao's daughter Mei Ying from Hengtangtou. Recently, because of lost love, he committed suicide by drinking brine. The Hangzhou Local Court has arrested Liang to inquire whether there are any other circumstances. (3) Shen Gengui, a native of Xiaoshan, was 73 years old, poor, old, and helpless. He committed suicide by hanging himself from a tree in Hupao Temple. After someone rescued him and inquired about the facts, he was given three yuan and told not to commit suicide. (4) Wu Xiangfu, a native of Dantu, was unemployed in Hangzhou, and all his belongings were pawned. He was stranded in a foreign land and committed suicide by jumping into the West Lake in Lakeside Park. He was rescued by the police and sent to the Public Security Bureau for verification.

Specials

Overview of Trade in Gansu Province in the Recent Three Years 93

— Zhu Jingzhou

I

The health of a country's economy can always be discerned from its imports and exports. A trade surplus or deficit is indicative, for a country with a trade deficit will inevitably experience a large outflow of cash. The result often undermines the economic foundation. Although China's current panic is significantly related to the U.S. silver purchase policy, the fundamental fatal wound remains the annual trade deficit of approximately 700 million yuan. This necessitates the export of a large amount of cash to offset the deficit. In the past, China relied on substantial remittances from overseas Chinese (estimated by American scholar Remer at approximately 316 million yuan in 1930. According to Zhu Jingzhou's investigation in 1927, remittances from overseas Chinese in the British and Dutch colonies alone to Xiamen, Shantou, and Guangzhou amounted to around 200 million yuan annually. If we include Europe, America, Australia, the Philippines, Siam, Annam, Yangon, Taiwan, Japan, and Korea, the amount would be between 400 and 500 million yuan). This helped to offset a large portion of the deficit, thus limiting the outflow of cash. However, since the global economic downturn, overseas Chinese have faced bankruptcies and are barely able to survive, leaving no surplus to remit back to China. Furthermore, there have been unfortunate incidents of discrimination against Chinese in South America and Japan. The sole means of offsetting the trade deficit in the past has now completely vanished, leaving no alternative but to transport cash. Thus, year after year, the outflow of domestic cash has increased. Even without the U.S. silver purchase policy, it would be impossible to sustain. However, the silver policy, which raised the price of silver, is even more detrimental to China's export trade, akin to a death warrant. In short, the nationwide rural bankruptcy and collapse of the economic foundation are the culmination of years of massive trade deficits, not a sudden occurrence.

II

As mentioned above, the trade balance is crucial to a country's economy. The same principle applies to a province. What was the state of trade in Gansu Province in the past? Without statistics, it is impossible to know. Since taking office, Zhu Jingzhou has recognized the importance of these statistics. He has classified and calculated various tax tickets from the Provincial Treasury's revenue items, starting from 1932. In that year, the total value of import and export trade was 60,699,307 yuan, with exports accounting for 14,656,196 yuan and imports accounting for 46,043,111 yuan, resulting in a trade deficit of 31,386,915 yuan. In 1933, the total value of import and export trade was 80,000,472 yuan, with exports accounting for 15,415,467 yuan and imports accounting for 64,585,005 yuan, resulting in a trade deficit of 49,169,538 yuan. In 1934, the total value of import and export trade was 63,653,989 yuan, with exports accounting for 2,252,372 yuan and imports accounting for 42,401,617 yuan, resulting in a trade deficit of 21,149,245 yuan. In total, the export value was highest in 1934 and lowest in 1932. The import value was highest in 1933 and lowest in 1934. The trade deficit was also highest in 1933. The total export value for the three years was only 51,324,035 yuan, while the total import value reached 153,029,733 yuan. The total trade deficit was 101,705,698 yuan (this import and export trade largely includes Qinghai). It is about twice the export value, which means that in addition to bearing various taxes, the people of Gansu Province had to spend a large amount of money on the trade deficit during these three years. Before the separation of Ningxia and Qinghai provinces, Gansu was known to have a population of 9 million. After the separation, it is estimated to be no more than 7 million. In recent years, due to natural disasters and man-made calamities, death, and migration, the population has sharply declined. According to the revised edition of the Encyclopedia of Daily Use published by the Commercial Press in 1932, the population of Gansu Province in 1932 was only 5,762,109, which seems more reliable. Based on this, the average burden for each person over the three years is slightly over 17.8 yuan, or slightly under 6 yuan per person per year. According to general opinion, the only way to offset this trade deficit is through the export of special products. However, since this year, a five-year ban has been implemented, with the first phase covering thirteen counties, including Gaolan, which has already been implemented. The economy of the people of Gansu Province will be in an increasingly precarious state. The reason why the trade deficit in 1934 was more than 28 million yuan less than in 1933 can be attributed to the following factors: (1) Rural bankruptcy, the social economy is declining, people's purchasing power is decreasing, stores cannot sell their inventory, and imports are also shrinking. (2) Gansu's economy has been based on the special product trade, but since 1934, due to the central government's widespread ban on opium, prices have plummeted, merchants have no profit to make, and they are all waiting and watching, resulting in a decline in imports.

III

In summary, there are several noteworthy points regarding the trade situation in Gansu Province during the aforementioned two years. These are discussed separately for imports and exports. (1) Imports: Among the imports, excluding miscellaneous goods, the most important items are cloth and cotton. In 1932, they were valued at 4,874,680 yuan, accounting for 10.58% of the total import value. In 1933, they were valued at 7,167,234 yuan, accounting for 11.11% of the total import value. In 1934, they were valued at 4,839,441 yuan, accounting for 11.43% of the total import value. Next is tea, including both official tea and loose tea (Gansu has tea permits, similar to salt permits in Jiangnan, called official tea. Tea traded freely by the people is called loose tea). In 1932, it was 2,353,040 yuan, accounting for 5.12% of the total import value. In 1933, it was 2,057,690 yuan, accounting for 3.19% of the total import value. In 1934, it was 1,769,126 yuan, accounting for 4.18% of the total import value. Next is paper. In 1932, it was valued at 1,269,950 yuan, accounting for 2.76% of the total import value. In 1933, it was valued at 1,561,320 yuan, accounting for 2.57% of the total import value. In 1934, it was valued at 1,973,620 yuan, accounting for 4.67% of the total import value. Next is food. In 1932, it was valued at 623,000 yuan, accounting for 1.35% of the total import value. In 1933, it was valued at 810,000 yuan, accounting for 1.25% of the total import value. In 1934, it was valued at 826,000 yuan, accounting for 1.95% of the total import value. (Appendix tables omitted). (2) Exports: Fur is the largest export. In 1932, it was valued at 7,088,670 yuan, accounting for 48.37% of the total export value. In 1933, it was valued at 6,640,172 yuan, accounting for 43.08% of the total export value. In 1934, it was valued at 10,058,197 yuan, accounting for 52.01% of the total export value. Next are medicinal materials. In 1932, they were valued at 4,879,155 yuan, accounting for 33.29% of the total export value. In 1933, they were valued at 6,119,777 yuan, accounting for 39.75% of the total export value. In 1934, they were valued at 7,058,856 yuan, accounting for 33.22% of the total export value. Next is water pipe tobacco. In 1932, it was valued at 1,175,099 yuan, accounting for 8.84% of the total export value. In 1933, it was valued at 2,217,099 yuan, accounting for 14.41% of the total export value. In 1934, it was valued at 1,841,701 yuan, accounting for 8.67% of the total export value. (Appendix tables omitted).

IV

The reason for China's trade deficit can be summarized in two words: "more consumption than production." Therefore, to reduce the trade deficit, we should strive for the development of various industries and take practical actions. The same applies to Gansu Province. Now, let's elaborate on the points discussed in the previous section.

(1) Promote cotton planting: The top import to Gansu Province each year is cloth and cotton. In the recent three years, the average annual import value is estimated to be over 9.6 million yuan, which is a significant outflow. The Northwest has a vast area suitable for cotton cultivation. At this time of phased opium prohibition, we must make every effort to promote it. The Central Cotton Improvement Institute has already allocated 200 dan of seeds. This issue can be said to be under development and will soon have significant results, which can be reported to those concerned about the Northwest problem.

(2) Promote small-scale papermaking: Paper is also a major import to Gansu Province, and it is increasing every year, reaching around 300,000 yuan. This is a good sign of the increasing cultural development in Gansu. If the weather is favorable and transportation is convenient, the demand will increase, and it will inevitably replace cloth and cotton. The Longnan and Longxi areas are rich in papermaking materials. A detailed survey should be conducted, and a simple introduction to papermaking should be printed to encourage people to imitate and manufacture freely, in order to save the situation.

(3) Open wool and leather factories: According to the export statistics of Gansu Province in the recent three years, fur production accounts for nearly 48%. If we only consider 1934, it accounts for over 52% of the total export trade. Its importance is evident. Fur is not only needed for ordinary clothing, but also has great value in military affairs. Since the fall of the Northeast, we rely solely on the Northwest. However, this matter is significant and requires a large-scale plan to succeed. Gansu Province has exhausted its financial resources after the devastation and may not be able to undertake this.

(4) Establish pharmaceutical factories: The output of medicinal materials is the second most important export in Gansu Province. The average export volume in the recent three years accounts for nearly 33% of the total and is increasing daily. Gansu Province produces the most medicinal materials, and the most famous ones are rhubarb, licorice, angelica, astragalus, etc. If factories can be established to manufacture locally, a considerable amount of outflow can be recovered. In recent years, the import of Western medicine has become a serious problem, and Westerners have made pills and tablets from rhubarb and angelica, which are sold exclusively in China. There is an urgent need to catch up.

(5) Promote tobacco planting: Lanzhou water pipe tobacco has been famous at home and abroad for a long time. According to Xu Peihuang, a German tested Lanzhou tobacco leaves and found that the cigars made from them were superior to those from Luzon, which shows the excellent quality. It has always occupied an important position in the history of Gansu's export trade. In recent years, due to changes in domestic preferences and excessive tax burdens, it has been declining year by year. According to the International Trade Bureau, the number of tobacco leaves imported nationwide in 1934 was 15.75 million gold units, which is alarming. If we can improve the seeds and expand the area, it will not be difficult to restore the past glory of Lanzhou water pipe tobacco. It will be able to reappear its active position in the export trade. The above is a fundamental plan to reverse Gansu's trade deficit. A plan should be established and implemented step by step. In a few years, the trade deficit will decrease naturally, and the national economy will have a prosperous future. This depends on the efforts of the Chinese people. As for the current palliative measures, the Provincial Treasury is revising the consumption tax rate with the following guidelines: (1) The import tax rate will be increased, and the export tax rate will be reduced. (2) Within the import tax rate, the tax rate on foreign goods will be increased, and the tax rate on domestic goods will be reduced. The tax rate on luxury goods will be increased, and the tax rate on necessities will be reduced, in order to remedy the situation for the time being. If this continues year after year, the entire economy of Gansu will be plunged into decline. Therefore, we have no choice but to adopt this tax policy for self-defense. (Concise table of import and export trade in Gansu Province in the recent three years omitted)

He Bingxian Discusses Developing Overseas Trade; Establishing Agencies in Various Overseas Locations; Specializing in Introducing Domestic Goods and Promoting Them Overseas 96

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, He Bingxian, Director of the International Trade Bureau, recently took a train to Nanjing to meet with Chen Gongbo, Minister of Industry, to discuss strategies for developing foreign trade. He has now completed his official business and returned to Shanghai by train yesterday morning. A reporter from Xin Xin News Agency interviewed He at the International Trade Bureau yesterday and discussed the situation as follows:

Visiting Minister Chen to Discuss Developing Trade

According to He, he went to Nanjing to meet with Minister Chen to discuss the basic strategies for developing foreign trade. He also reported on the progress of guiding domestic goods manufacturers in Shanghai to voluntarily organize industrial and trade associations. Minister Chen has instructed the relevant departments to prepare for the implementation of measures to balance international trade. He expressed great approval for the establishment of industrial and trade associations by domestic goods factories in Shanghai, believing that this is an essential step in developing China's foreign trade. He instructed He to do his best to guide them so that they can be established as soon as possible. He plans to meet with the founders of the association tomorrow (today) to inquire about the preparation status and guide the progress.

Establishing Agencies to Introduce Domestic Goods

He denied the rumor that the Ministry of Industry will jointly form an international trade committee with relevant ministries to study ways to balance international trade. According to him, he had absolutely not heard of any such plan from the Ministry of Industry during his stay in Nanjing. It is difficult to find out where the above news came from. When asked whether the International Trade Bureau has specific measures to develop overseas trade, he replied that the reasons for China's foreign trade slump are multifaceted. However, the lack of knowledge about Chinese goods among overseas people, which makes it impossible for them to purchase them, is also a major reason. The Bureau is currently in contact with the industrial and commercial sectors and leaders of overseas Chinese in various places to establish domestic goods agencies in various overseas locations, specializing in introducing domestic goods. In addition, it will also set up domestic goods exhibition halls in various parts of Nanyang so that overseas people have a deep understanding of Chinese goods.

Details of Anti-Chinese Sentiment in the Dutch East Indies Are Unknown

In his last answer to the Xin Xin News Agency reporter's question, He said that the government had not yet received a detailed report when he was in Nanjing regarding reports that the government of the Dutch East Indies has recently abused overseas Chinese. The true situation is currently unknown. However, when Dutch East Indies Minister of Economic Affairs Hart visited Shanghai last month, he met with him and discussed how to promote the development of bilateral trade. At that time, Hart's attitude was quite sincere. If the Dutch East Indies government does have anti-Chinese incidents, Hart's words after returning should be more moderate.

Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau Starts Rural Lending; Kunshan Office Established; Ministry of Communications Approves Lending Outline 97

In order to develop the rural economy, the Ministry of Communications conducted a trial rural loan in Hunan Province last year with excellent results. This year, it decided to expand the scope of the loan and first conduct trials in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces. All lending plans and implementation outlines have been drafted by the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau and submitted to the Ministry for approval. An office in Kunshan has already been established, and other locations can be established in order. Staff have been sent out for inspection. The details are as follows:

Sending Staff for Inspection

The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau sent Director Shen, Secretary Wang, and others to various places for inspection. Now, the Bureau has sent Secretary Wang to Jiaxing, Huzhou, and other places to continue the inspection in order to start establishing lending offices and start lending to farmers. Wang will set off in the next few days. According to Secretary Wang's statement to the Guomin News Agency reporter, these offices are divided into two types: Type A offices will temporarily use a standard of 200,000 loans, and Type B offices will lend 100,000 yuan. They will be established according to the needs of rural areas. However, if the amount of this loan is required by the environment, it can also be changed slightly.

Preparing to Establish Offices in Various Counties

After the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau received the order from the Ministry of Communications to conduct trial rural loans in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces, it began to prepare and actively carry out the work. Director Wang of the Bureau and Secretary Wang went to rural areas in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces for inspection. After returning to the Bureau, they drafted an implementation outline and submitted it to the Ministry for approval. The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau immediately began to prepare for the establishment of lending offices in various counties. An office in Kunshan has already been established a few days ago. Offices in other places, such as Taicang and Yixing, are also actively underway and will soon be established.

Lending Outline

The Bureau has also drafted a rural lending outline, which has been approved by the Ministry of Communications. The outline is as follows: (1) For the convenience of external understanding and general recognition, the name of the rural lending should be named the "Rural Lending Office of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau" and the name of the location should be prefixed to the office; (2) The guidelines for rural lending are as follows: There are two difficulties in rural lending: one is that genuine farmers cannot benefit from the loan, and at the same time, cumbersome procedures must be avoided; the other is that agricultural product production and sales are time-sensitive, and the establishment of lending institutions and pledge procedures should be noted. In terms of lending targets, it should be producers of agricultural products and merchants who are directly related to farmers, so that the effect of universal relief can be achieved. As for the lending method, at the beginning of the trial, pledge should be handled first, followed by agency savings and pledge remittance, and then agency savings and pledge remittance, so that the procedure has a consistent chain; (3) The steps for rural lending are as follows: Rural lending is a government policy to relieve rural areas. In order to facilitate the implementation of the Bureau and to make farmers understand the lending content, in addition to setting up propaganda items by the Bureau in public places, we will contact the local government so that the autonomous organizations in each township and town can widely publicize it to achieve the universal effect of lending; (4) The area of rural lending, in order to facilitate the implementation and supervision, it is proposed to take the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, where transportation is convenient, agricultural products are abundant, and there is a need for lending, as the initial trial area, and gradually promote it as a principle, and those with certainty. In this trial area, Kunshan, Changshu, Taicang, Suzhou, Yixing, Wuxi, and Liyang in Jiangsu Province are the first phase, on the one hand, to train practical talents for the preparation of promotion, and on the other hand, to use the trial method to seek the steady progress of the business; (5) Omitted; (6) Omitted; (7) The stacks are either designated by the Bureau to act as stacks, and pledge is made with receipts, or the stacks are rented by the Bureau, and stack fees are collected from the pledgers. At the same time, the Bureau plans to build warehouses in appropriate locations to achieve practical use.

The Various Shipping Companies Should Give Priority to Employing Local Seamen; the Captains' Association Submitted a Request to the Ministry Yesterday 101

Recently, various shipping companies have frequently employed foreign seamen, which not only hinders our navigation rights but also causes local seamen to be squeezed out. The Merchant Ship Captains' Association yesterday submitted a special request to the Ministry, asking it to order various shipping companies to give priority to employing local seamen and not to hire foreigners. The original request is recorded below:

Submitting a request to order the Navigation Administration Bureau to instruct various shipping companies that, whenever there are opportunities to hire seamen, they should prioritize hiring local people to protect navigation rights and to provide relief to the unemployed.

Since China opened its ports to foreign trade, the crew members on merchant ships were initially mostly foreigners. This was because our country lacked nautical talent and had to rely on foreign resources, which resulted in the loss of sovereignty and the outflow of benefits, causing widespread grief. Fortunately, in recent years, the country has spared no effort in cultivating maritime talent. The graduates of merchant marine and fisheries schools, as well as those who have gained experience on merchant ships, are numerous enough to meet the needs of various vessels. Therefore, under the current circumstances, there is no need to employ foreigners any longer.

However, it has been recently observed that while some shipping companies are employing local seamen out of consideration for national rights, many others, disregarding the overall situation, still prefer to employ foreigners. Sometimes, they even go to great lengths to help foreigners without certificates pass through customs, while qualified local people with certificates are turned away, resulting in increasing unemployment. This is truly regrettable.

It is noted that the third extension of the seamen examination period will expire in June of this year. From then on, the seamen employed by companies should be judged by their certificates, and among seamen with certificates, priority should be given to employing local people. If this is done, unemployed local people with certificates can be helped, and the country's navigation rights can be gradually recovered.

Therefore, it is urgently requested that your Ministry order the Navigation Administration Bureau to instruct various shipping companies that, whenever there are opportunities to hire seamen, they should prioritize hiring local people. It is hoped that this request will be approved and implemented promptly for the public good. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Communications.

Another request states: Submitting a request for strict crackdown on seamen without certificates and for no further extension of the seamen examination period to maintain the rule of law.

Since the implementation of the seamen examination by your Ministry, nearly two years have passed. Those who comply with the law should have applied for the examination long ago, and those who pass should have certificates. Those who fail should not be allowed to perform their duties. This is the authority of the national law. In the past, your Ministry, considering the large number of seamen and the potential difficulty in examining all of them at once, has issued repeated extensions for the seamen examination. This was indeed out of genuine concern for the seamen, which is deeply appreciated. However, it has been recently observed that many seamen without certificates are still working safely, while many seamen with certificates are unemployed. This is certainly not the original intention of your Ministry's seamen examination.

It is noted that the third extension of the seamen examination period will expire in June of this year. Therefore, it is urgently requested that your Ministry refrain from granting any further extensions after this period expires so that unemployed seamen with certificates can be helped, and the authority of the national law can be maintained. It is truly for the public good. Respectfully submitted.

The Municipal Party Headquarters Strictly Orders All Levels of Party Branches to Vigorously Promote the Literacy Education Movement, and Orders All Organizations to Establish Literacy Schools; it is Estimated that 100,000 Illiterate People Can Be Eliminated in a Few Months 102

The Municipal Party Headquarters regards literacy education as one of the Party's seven major movements, and it is also the most effective way to improve public intelligence and revive culture. Now that the government is implementing it, mobilizing the entire social force is necessary to achieve the effect of division of labor and cooperation. Therefore, it was decided at the 169th Standing Committee meeting to organize a Literacy Education Promotion Association to coordinate the work and appoint Tong Xingbai, Wang Yansong, Li Suixian, Lin Meiyan, and Lu Jingshi as directors, with Tong Xingbai designated as the managing director.

The association has held several meetings and decided to promote literacy education in two ways: one is to be handled by party branches at all levels, with each of the ten districts and over two hundred sub-branches in the city establishing one school each. Each school will have two classes in the morning and afternoon, teaching one hundred people, totaling 20,000 people. The city has 7,000 party members, and each member is required to teach two people, totaling 14,000 people. The other way is to be promoted by various organizations. There are over 600 approved organizations in the city, such as agricultural, industrial, commercial, academic, and social and cultural groups. Each organization will establish one school, teaching one hundred people each, totaling over 80,000 people in the city. In total, over 110,000 illiterate people can be eliminated in February and March.

This is a general outline of the plan. It is heard that the Municipal Party Headquarters is determined to adopt an absolutely strict approach. Any party branch or organization that has the ability to hold literacy classes but delays or fails to implement them will be immediately disbanded or have its负责人(responsible person) replaced to serve as a warning to those with lax organization and poor leadership. At the same time, it is seeking the consent of the Bureau of Social Affairs to issue joint instructions, and will convene discussion meetings with various party branches and organizations in stages to actively promote literacy education. The details are recorded separately below:

Strict Orders for Preparations: For compliance. Literacy education is one of the seven major movements of our party, and it is also the most essential way to improve public intelligence. All comrades should exhaust their resources and talents to achieve this great undertaking. Now that the government is actively promoting it, we should serve the party and mobilize the entire population to achieve the effect of division of labor and cooperation. In view of this, our association has specially formulated two methods: "Methods for Party Branches at All Levels to Promote Literacy Education" and "Methods for Party Members to Promote Literacy Education." In addition to issuing a notice to all district party branches and sub-branches for compliance, we are also printing and distributing attachments for the sub-branches to comply with. From the date of receipt of this document, you are required to make preparations within two weeks, report them at any time, and open schools by June 20. Meanwhile, the executive committee member of the sub-branch is required to attend the Shangwen Elementary School on Penglai Road at 3:00 pm on the 18th of this month to receive instructions. Be sure to comply with this order.

Orders to Various Organizations: The Municipal Party Headquarters will use the existence and success of literacy schools as a standard to assess whether the organizations of various groups in the city are sound. It has already sought the consent of the Bureau of Social Affairs and issued joint instructions as follows:

For joint instructions: Literacy education is the most fundamental and essential way to promote public intelligence and revive culture. All citizens should exhaust their resources and talents to achieve this great undertaking. Now that the government is actively promoting it, it is impossible to achieve the effect of simultaneous efforts without mobilizing the entire social force. Moreover, various social organizations have the nature of serving the community and should bear the obligation of supporting public welfare. In view of this, our association and bureau have specially formulated two methods: "Methods for Various Organizations to Establish Literacy Schools" and "Implementation Methods." In addition to issuing a notice to all affiliated social organizations for compliance, we are also printing and distributing attachments for the association to comply with. From the date of receipt of this document, you are required to make preparations within two weeks, report them at any time, and open schools by June 20. Meanwhile, one responsible representative should be sent to the Shangwen Elementary School on Penglai Road at 9:00 am on the 19th of this month to receive a report. Be sure to comply with this order.

Convening Meetings: The Municipal Party Headquarters believes that the preparatory period has begun. Although various methods have been formulated, it is still necessary to convene separate meetings to explain the significance and methods of promoting literacy education in detail so that everyone can understand and achieve the effect of simultaneous efforts. Therefore, it is scheduled to convene a meeting of the executive committee members of each district branch at 3:00 pm on the 18th of this month and a meeting of the responsible representatives of various groups at 9:00 am on the 19th of this month at the Shangwen Elementary School on Penglai Road to hold important gatherings and provide as much instruction as possible.

Teacher Registration: When various groups hold literacy schools, they will need many teachers. Without careful selection, it will be enough to affect the prospects of literacy education. Therefore, a specific period is designated for literacy teacher registration. The original text of the proposed method is as follows:

Methods for Registering Literacy Education Teachers:

Article 1: Anyone who wants to be a literacy school teacher on behalf of the Shanghai Literacy Education Promotion Association should apply for registration according to this method.

Article 2: Anyone who has received considerable education and is willing to be a teacher in a literacy school established by various organizations must apply to the Municipal Party Headquarters Literacy Education Promotion Association for registration. Only those who pass the review are allowed to serve.

Article 3: Anyone who has one of the following qualifications may apply for registration: 1. Graduates of junior high school or junior normal school or above with certificates; 2. Students who have studied in junior high school or junior normal school for more than two years and have been teachers for more than three years with proof; 3. Those who have served as teachers in private elementary schools registered in Shanghai for more than one year with proof; 4. Those who have passed the literacy education committee examination; 5. Those who have rich teaching experience with proof.

Article 4: Application forms can be obtained from the Municipal Party Headquarters Literacy Education Promotion Association.

Article 5: Literacy teachers applying for registration must fill in their name, age, native place, address, background, experience, and thoughts on literacy education, etc., item by item according to the prescribed format, without omission.

Article 6: When applying for registration, two 4-inch half-length photos must be prepared, along with a graduation certificate or a school appointment letter, and submitted together for review.

Article 7: Literacy teachers who apply for registration and pass the review will be issued certificates by the Municipal Party Headquarters.

Article 8: Literacy teachers who pass the review will be notified in turn to serve when the Promotion Association holds literacy schools. However, there are no restrictions when there are no positions.

Article 9: The salary of registered literacy teachers who have positions is stipulated as follows: Type A schools are divided into two classes in the morning and afternoon, with more than 70 students in each class, teaching for two hours a day, with a salary and office expenses of 45 yuan per month; Type B schools are divided into two classes in the morning and afternoon, with more than 50 students in each class, teaching for two hours a day, with a salary and office expenses of 40 yuan per month; Type C schools are divided into two classes in the morning and afternoon, with more than 30 students in each class, teaching for two hours a day, with a salary and office expenses of 35 yuan per month.

Article 10: These methods shall be implemented after being approved by the Municipal Executive Committee.

Article 11: These methods may be amended at any time if there are any incomplete matters.

Anthropologist Dr. Schmidt Arrives in Shanghai 106

According to the North China Daily News, Dr. Schmidt, an internationally renowned scholar, was among the passengers when the Dollar Steamship Company's ship President Grant arrived in Shanghai from Japan today (14th). Dr. Schmidt was originally German, but has now been naturalized as Austrian. He is recognized as one of the leading contemporary anthropologists. Dr. Schmidt is a pastor of the Steyl Mission. While in Shanghai, he plans to stay briefly at the Shanghai branch agent of the church at 709 Avenue Joffre at Pastor Schürr's residence, and then plans to go north to the former capital to give several lectures. Dr. Schmidt has received honorary degrees from many universities around the world. He was one of the first to explore the languages of Australia and helped found the school of cultural history in anthropology. Dr. Schmidt has a deep understanding and outstanding achievements in comparative religion and the psychology of primitive religions. Therefore, important European societies have hired him as a member. Dr. Schmidt is also a director of the Lateran Museum in Rome. He came east from the United States and stayed in Japan for about a week. He originally planned to go directly to Peiping from Japan. Shanghai only received news yesterday that Dr. Schmidt had changed his itinerary. After arriving in Peiping, he will stay for several months and then go to Manila via Shanghai. Dr. Schmidt will lecture on his academic research in Peiping, such as the totemic system, the monotheism of primitive peoples, the belief in souls, and the art of witchcraft.

Two Methods to Attract Tea Chest Transport 109

Last year, the Carriage Department of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau amended and approved a special rebate method for transporting tea chests on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway to encourage the transport of tea chests. Any merchant who transports tea chests from the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo line, the Nanjing, Hangzhou, Gengshanmen, and Gongchenqiao stations directly to the Qibeinan Rihuigang station, and who has registered a brand name with the railway in advance and paid a tea chest transport deposit of 500 yuan, will be given a special rebate at the end of each year according to the following standards. However, those who have already received a special rebate will not enjoy the ordinary rebate. Annual transport volume exceeding 50,000 chests: 1.5%; exceeding 100,000 chests: 3%; exceeding 150,000 chests: 3.5%; exceeding 100,000 chests: 4%; exceeding 250,000 chests: 5%. Now that the tea chest season has arrived, the company has stipulated that for tea chests arriving at the Maigen Road station, the freight rate will be calculated in the same way as for those arriving at the Upper North Station, and the specified weight of each chest and the special rebate method will also be handled according to the established plan.

The Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Committee of the Republic of China Lawyers Association held a general meeting on the 5th of this month at the Suzhou Wuxian Lawyers Association, where it determined the draft principles of the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Law and elected Shen Junru, Dai Tianqiu, Chen Dexin, Chen Yaodong, Wu Zengshan, Li Shirui, Huang Weishi, and others as review committee members. Shipping Representatives Request Expansion of the Dredging Plan and Removal of滩艒艒(Tan Nu Nu) boats along the Beach 111

Xing Zhigang, a shipping representative from Pudong West, submitted a request to the Shanghai Municipal Government yesterday to expand the Shanghai South District dredging plan, remove obstacles along the beach, and reorganize water traffic to maintain the safety of navigation and travel. The document stated:

I submitted two requests in December 1933 and September 1934 to dredge the shoal from Dongjiadu to the South Wharf and remove obstacles along the beach. In response, your office approved the dredging section, which will be dredged around 1935. As for the request to remove obstacles along the area south of Dongjiadu, an order should be issued to the Public Security and Public Works Bureaus to investigate and handle the matter.

This year happens to be the time of the Huaihe River flooding season. Dredging has already reached the Bund outside the Wanjin Wharf. However, it is heard that this dredging will only extend to the Dongjiadu Wharf, and the area south of Dongjiadu is still not included in the plan. The area north of Dongjiadu is the area that should be dredged in the port, and the dock management office of the Public Works Bureau is already reorganizing it, so I do not need to discuss it further. However, the area south of Dongjiadu is currently a prosperous port for cargo loading and unloading for ships from various towns and villages in Shanghai, Fengxian, Nanhui, and Chuansha counties. It is also a place for large and small civilian ships to rush to dock. Now, bamboo, wood, and tree rafts are blocking half of the river, slowing the tide and current, and accumulating sand. If dredging is not carried out quickly, the harm to navigation will be significant. Furthermore, 滩艒艒(Tan Nu Nu) boats along the beach are crowding the port, hindering traffic. Cargo ships cannot dock and are forced to go far into the river, where they are hit by strong tides and accidents frequently occur. I have personally experienced this situation and cannot remain silent.

Therefore, I dare to repeat my previous request and urge you to examine the situation carefully and order the Public Works, Public Utilities, and Public Security Bureaus to take advantage of this dredging of neighboring ports and extend it to the South Wharf, uniformly deepening the area and removing the 滩艒艒(Tan Nu Nu) boats and obstacles along the beach to improve the waterway traffic on the Huangpu River and maintain the safety of navigation and travel. I would be extremely grateful.

Bean and Rice Industry Presents a Report: Proposed Measures for Opening Cuixiu Hall 113

The municipal government, in order to provide public access to the gardens within the city temple for sightseeing purposes, specifically instructed the Social Affairs Bureau to direct the relevant trade associations to discuss measures for opening them. Regarding the Cuixiu Hall, the Bean and Rice Trade Association has, after deliberation, drafted measures for opening it and submitted them to the Social Affairs Bureau. The original text submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau is excerpted below. Respectfully to the Director of the Bureau: We respectfully report that we previously received letter No. 3493 from your bureau, forwarded by the Bean and Rice Trade Association, which stated: Based on Municipal Government Instruction No. 3611, it has been found that the city temple is a must-see destination for both domestic and foreign visitors to Shanghai. However, the Dianchun Hall, Cuixiu Hall, and the three gardens within, which are exemplary of the inherent architectural spirit of our nation, have not been open to the public due to their association with various trade associations. This is regrettable, and leaders of the relevant trades should be contacted immediately to facilitate their opening for public viewing. In addition to separate instructions to the Public Security and Public Works Bureaus, the said bureau is hereby instructed to comply accordingly, to consult together, to set a deadline for opening, and to report on the progress of compliance. Upon receiving this instruction, we acknowledge that the fact that the temple gardens are not open to the public is indeed regrettable and that efforts should be made to open them for public viewing. It has been decided to hold a meeting at the Cuixiu Hall in the city temple at [time missing] PM on April 23rd. We respectfully request your attendance and participation in the discussion. Subsequently, at the designated time on April 23rd, a meeting was convened at our association's Cuixiu Hall by your bureau, bringing together representatives from various relevant agencies and organizations. The meeting resulted in a decision that representatives from the three industries would first convene their respective members to discuss the principles of opening to the public. They would then report the results of these meetings to your bureau before May 15th for further discussion. This has been recorded. Our association, in compliance, convened a meeting of all its members on May 9th. After serious deliberation, it was unanimously agreed that our association's Cuixiu Hall was established during the Daoguang reign of the Qing Dynasty. At that time, Yuyuan Garden had been neglected for many years and was in a state of disrepair. The Shanghai County Magistrate invited merchants to undertake repairs, stipulating that each trade manage specific areas as meeting places for their associations. Our bean and rice merchants undertook the repair of Sansui Hall, Cuixiu Hall, and other areas. Several years later, they purchased a portion of the site of the Kele Xuan and Wanhua Lou, namely the area around the Shenchi Tang, and established it as the association's headquarters. During the Taiping Rebellion in the Xianfeng reign, Western troops were stationed there, and the damage from one incident was particularly severe. Over the following years, repairs were carried out. The large artificial mountain in Sansui Hall was renovated in the seventh year of the Tongzhi reign. During the Qing Dynasty land survey, after the land was measured and mapped, the county magistrate issued an edict for bearing the land tax, and a stone tablet was erected to commemorate this. This arrangement has remained unchanged to this day. When our industry merged with other industries to form a trade association, this place was also used as the association's headquarters. For decades, members of our industry have used this headquarters not only for gatherings to discuss market conditions, study trade regulations, deliberate on public welfare, and manage association affairs, but also for the quarterly calibration of measuring instruments used by members. Furthermore, a school was established near Sansui Hall to promote education. All of these endeavors have been possible thanks to this headquarters. In recent years, due to the increasing complexity of association affairs and the expansion of the school, there are concerns that the space may be insufficient. As for the large artificial mountain, which has long been renowned for its scenic beauty, since the western buildings were converted into a playground and the area around the Nine-Bend Bridge to the south was opened to the bustle of the city, ascending it now offers nothing but a chaotic and disruptive view, and no longer resembles the tranquility of a mountain forest in the city. Moreover, the mountain rocks are rugged and uneven, and the paths are winding and narrow. While a small number of people can still wander around, it is doubtful whether it is suitable for the enjoyment of a large number of people. Therefore, our industry has carefully considered the matter of opening the Hall to the public, and we genuinely feel that there are significant obstacles. However, we admire the City Government and your bureau for thinking of the public and creating areas for sightseeing, which is something that everyone supports, and our industry is especially in agreement. Therefore, how could our industry not strive to comply with public sentiment and uphold your intentions? We have, in the face of these obstacles, devised a method of adaptation. The members of our industry have decided to voluntarily open the hall to the public for one day each week, taking advantage of the school's holidays. However, as our association has a school in the front and a headquarters in the back, the areas open to the public must be demarcated, and the large artificial mountain is winding and difficult to navigate, and precautions must be taken to prevent accidents, thus some regulations are necessary. These two points still require detailed planning by the organizing management committee, and further details will be submitted in due course. We are now submitting the results of the discussions among our industry members in this letter, respectfully requesting your consideration. With utmost respect, we wish you good health. Shanghai Bean Industry Cuixiu Hall.

According to the Dagong News Agency, the Shanghai office of the National Government Aviation Highway Construction Lottery announced yesterday that it has decided to change the lottery's prize amounts starting from the fourteenth issue and to add two first, second, and third prize bonus prizes. This will be implemented after approval from the Central Political Council. The details are as follows:

Changing the Policy: Since its inception, the aviation lottery has enjoyed a strong reputation. Sales for the twelfth issue recently closed, with over 300,000 to 400,000 tickets sold. A Dagong News Agency reporter recently heard rumors that the office was planning to change its policy and increase the prize amounts starting from the fourteenth issue. Yesterday, the reporter visited Mr. Sun Disheng, the chief of the office's First Section, who stated that the office had previously discussed increasing the lottery's prize amounts, but this had not been implemented due to certain reasons. While the current proposal is still under consideration, the general outlines have been decided. The office will submit a formal request to the Ministry of Finance, which will then forward it to the Executive Yuan for submission to the Central Political Council. The changes could be implemented as early as the next issue, or as late as the fourteenth issue.

Increasing Prize Amounts: Regarding the prize amounts, the office plans to increase the first prize to 250,000 yuan for the sake of greater popularity, and add two first prize bonus prizes of 5,000 yuan each. Two second and third prize bonus prizes will also be added. In addition, the office plans to modestly increase the value of other smaller prizes by tens of thousands of yuan. Regarding the price of tickets, the office does not wish to sharply increase the price, as it wishes to encourage the public to take an interest in aviation and highway construction. However, while the office has reached an agreement on these points, they are still subject to the approval of the authorities, and it is uncertain whether these changes will be approved. The office is currently preparing the formal request, which will be submitted to the Ministry of Finance within the next day or two.

Hebei Native Place Association Petitions for Extension of Yellow River Disaster Lottery for Another Year 115

The Hebei Native Place Association has submitted a document to the Executive Yuan and Ministry of Finance of the National Government, petitioning for the extension of the Yellow River disaster lottery for another year to raise funds for disaster relief. The document states: This association has recently received representatives from the Yellow River disaster area in southern Hebei, Tian Jianai, Guan Zhaofeng, and others, representing hundreds of thousands of people from southern Hebei. They stated that since August of the 22nd year of the Republic [1933], the Yellow River has flooded, with torrential waters breaching both the north and south banks of Changyuan County in southern Hebei. As a result, the three counties of Chang, Pu, and Dong were instantly turned into a swamp. The severity of the disaster and the scale of the losses are unprecedented. Subsequently, due to the lack of a steady stream of disaster relief funds from various sources, hundreds of thousands of disaster victims were left starving, and the various post-disaster measures in the disaster area were urgently needed. As a last resort, in June of last year, the association petitioned the Peiping Political Readjustment Committee for permission to issue a Yellow River disaster lottery for one year to provide relief. The lottery was specifically established to provide relief for the Yellow River disaster of the 22nd year of the Republic and to carry out various post-disaster measures. Unexpectedly, not long after the lottery was launched, the Yellow River breached its banks again in Chang in August of last year, causing an unprecedented catastrophe and repeating the disaster a second time. The villagers of Chang, Pu, and other counties who were submerged in the floodwaters have now been suffering for ten months. The length of the disaster and the scale of the losses are even greater than the previous breach. Because Hebei Province is facing a severe financial crisis and sources of disaster relief funds from various sources have dried up, the only reason why the disaster victims in the three counties have not died of starvation or drowning is the 50,000 yuan of regular monthly income from the Yellow River disaster lottery. Although the Guantaikou gate has now been closed, the water has not completely receded, and there is no prospect of planting. Hundreds of thousands of disaster victims are still starving, and after the great disaster, the villagers in the disaster area have lost all their houses, property, livestock, and agricultural tools. The misery of the disaster is unparalleled, and the urgency of the need for help is immediate. It is now planned to continue providing relief to the hundreds of thousands of disaster victims to prevent them from dying, and to carefully plan for post-disaster recovery, handling agricultural goods, and restoring the countryside, so that the disaster victims can have the strength to cultivate and gradually recover and recuperate. In order to reverse the catastrophe, a total of at least 600,000 yuan is needed. The provincial government has exhausted its resources and has no way to raise this amount. The Yellow River disaster lottery will expire on the 15th of this month. If it is not continued, there will be no disaster relief funds, and all the above-mentioned relief and post-disaster recovery measures will inevitably be mere empty talk. The hundreds of thousands of disaster victims will still be displaced. We have always admired your association's concern for our hometown and ask for your support in appealing to the government. We believe that it is the government's responsibility to rescue those in distress. Since the provincial government's finances are exhausted, the central government should provide overall consideration and assistance. The Yellow River disaster lottery has a strong reputation and has achieved remarkable results. The current arrangement should be allowed to continue for another year to raise funds for disaster relief. Knowing this, how could this association remain silent? Therefore, we are presenting the above facts and earnestly requesting your Yuan (Ministry) to consider the disaster victims and to approve the extension of the Yellow River disaster lottery for another year, starting from the 15th of this month, to save the starving and drowning and to reverse the catastrophe. This would be in the public interest. Respectfully submitted to the Executive Yuan (Ministry of Finance) of the National Government by the Hebei Shanghai Native Place Association. Chairman: Hong Yi. Vice Chairman: Li Shizeng.

Import of Linen Fabric for Embroidery: Customs Notice on Application of Guarantee Measures 116

Tang Haian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Luo Fude, Commissioner of Customs, jointly issued Notice No. 1445 yesterday, stating: Regarding the measures for levying taxes on imported plain (i.e., unpatterned) pure linen fabric specifically used for drawn-thread embroidery and other similar handicrafts, notices No. 1310 of July 24, 1933, and No. 1392 of October 26, 1934, have already been issued. Now, we have received an order from the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance, stating that these tax levy measures are not limited to plain linen fabric. All linen fabric that has been verified by the Customs as being used for embroidery shall be subject to the guarantee measures and taxed at 7.5% ad valorem according to Tariff Item 104 of the import tariff. We hereby order compliance accordingly. This will be implemented starting on April 3rd of this year. All pure linen fabrics specifically used for embroidery and other similar handicrafts must be declared by merchants upon import with a guarantee (the guarantee form can be found in this Customs Notice No. 1310) as the basis for verification. This notice is hereby issued.

Parricide by Strangulation Case Adjudicated: Yu Huogen and His Daughter-in-Law Straightforwardly Admit to Strangulation: Pouring Out Grievances about the Son's Heinous Deeds, Old Man Weeps Copiously 125

Yu Huogen, a farmer from Yujiagang Township in the western part of Hexiang in the southwestern countryside, due to his rebellious son Yu Guanhong (i.e., Yu Jisheng)'s failure to engage in honest work, sinking into depravity, and addiction to red pills and morphine injections, stealing openly and covertly, and committing all kinds of evils, hated him to the bone. He colluded with his daughter-in-law, Yu Chen (i.e., Guanhong's wife), and strangled Guanhong to death with a rope on the night of the tenth day of the third month of the lunar calendar this year while he was asleep. After the incident, the police station detained and sent Yu Chen to the local court for interrogation and detention. Prosecutor Lei Binzhang arrived at the scene to examine the body and have it placed in a coffin. Yu Huogen was originally supposed to be arrested and detained, but because he was suffering from severe dropsy and was over sixty years old, he was handed over to the local headman for supervision. The magistrate prosecuted Yu Huogen and Yu Chen for violating Article 284, paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code and requested a public trial in the Criminal Court. It is now learned that this case was heard yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM by Judge Zhang Shao in the specially opened Fifth Court. Yu Chen, who was in custody, was brought to the stand. She testified that she was 34 years old and had one son and two daughters. Her husband, Yu Guanhong, was lazy and did not work. He was addicted to red pills and morphine injections. He would steal clothing and other items worth a little bit to sell and also steal clothing from other people's houses, as well as things planted in the fields. He also threatened to set fire to the house, which caused the whole family to suffer. Even if we went to court, this kind of bad person should be shot. Asked, "How exactly did your husband die?" She replied, "He was killed by my father-in-law (referring to Yu Huogen)." Asked, "Did you and your father-in-law kill him together?" She replied, "Yes." Asked, "Who caused the injuries on your husband's head?" She replied, "My father-in-law hit him. He was angry because he was unpromising and did not learn well, so my father-in-law became ill from anger." Asked, "Did your father-in-law discuss it with you beforehand?" She replied, "He told me several times. I couldn't bear to do it." Asked, "Then why did you still kill him?" She replied, "Because he said he would definitely set fire. I have been a child bride in this family since I was seven years old and have suffered all kinds of hardships." Asked, "How could you bear to kill your husband, with whom you have been married for so many years?" She replied, "He was stealing things all day long, and his face was gaunt." Asked, "How does your family survive?" She replied, "I earn money by making lace, supporting my father-in-law and three children. We eat two meals of thin porridge a day." When she testified, her eyes were filled with tears, and she looked extremely miserable. (She was wearing tattered clothes and looked timid, truly a poor village woman.) Next, Yu Huogen testified that he was 64 years old and had two sons. The eldest son was Guanhong, and the second son was Guansheng. The second son died of illness last spring, leaving behind a blind daughter-in-law. Asked, "Is Guanhong your biological son?" He replied, "Yes." Asked, "How many people were involved?" He replied, "I did it alone. I strangled him with a belt. I killed him while Guanhong was asleep. I got on the bed and sat on him and killed him. He stole things from the house and sold them, even tearing down and selling the bricks and tiles from the grave of his dead mother to fuel his addiction to red pills and morphine. Half of the house has been torn down, and the bricks and tiles have been continuously transported out and sold cheaply to support his red pill and morphine addiction." Asked, "Why didn't you send him to the vagrant work training center?" He replied, "I asked someone to introduce him, but the center was full and could not accommodate him, so he was rejected." Asked, "How did Guanhong treat you usually?" He replied, "He was extremely fierce and often beat me, even trying to kill me with a knife, claiming that killing his father would only get him three months in jail." Asked, "Is your daughter-in-law well-behaved?" He replied, "She is well-behaved. If you don't believe me, you can investigate. If she has any misbehavior, please have her shot." Asked, "Did you and your daughter-in-law discuss it beforehand?" He replied, "We talked about it once this year, and several times last year, because the rebellious son recently threatened to kill me, so I struck first." Asked, "Has your dropsy been relieved in recent days?" He replied, "I can't urinate, and my belly is as hard as a drum. This illness was also caused by anger," and so on. The magistrate ordered Chen Wentang, the local headman of the 28th district, to be brought to the stand and asked, "How is Yu Huogen as a person?" He replied, "Very good." Asked, "How is Yu Chen?" He replied, "Also good, usually very well-behaved, but very miserable." Asked, "How was the deceased as a person?" He replied, "The deceased was very bad. Stealing things, eating red pills, injecting morphine, committing all kinds of evils, he was really a scoundrel. I am willing to sign a guarantee." At this point, Prosecutor Lei Binzhang came to the court to make a statement, briefly stating that the defendants had confessed without reservation, and that Yu Huogen's actions were excusable. He asked for leniency. The appointed lawyer, Hu Yuanjun, then rose to defend them. The magistrate then asked Yu Huogen, "Who else is in your family?" He replied, "One grandson, nine years old, and two granddaughters, fourteen and eleven years old. Since my daughter-in-law was taken into custody, we have been without a livelihood. I go out to beg every day to support the three children." After he finished speaking, he wept copiously, moving those who heard him. The magistrate then asked the local headman, Chen Wentang, whether Yu Huogen's testimony was false. Chen replied, "It is indeed the truth." The magistrate felt compassion for them and announced the end of the arguments and ordered that a judgment would be issued later. He also instructed the local headman to take Yu Huogen back to be supervised, and Yu Chen was returned to custody to await further instructions.

At 3 p.m., the certificate presentation ceremony was held in the auditorium on the third floor, presided over by Dr. Patterson, the hospital director. Mrs. Li Yan'an presented the certificates. This year's graduates totaled thirty-four, mostly female, which is why Mr. Li's speech emphasized this.

At 3 o'clock, Chairman Dr. Bai announced the opening of the meeting, and the group sang the hymn "With the Lord." Dr. Bai spoke Chinese quite fluently, and when expressing his gratitude, he raised his hands in a traditional Chinese greeting, his sincere feelings overflowing in his words.

Renji Hospital Nursing School Graduation Ceremony

Two Points of Hope - The chairman hoped for two things from the graduating nurses. The general idea was: (1) Do not regard this graduation examination as the final test. In the future, when dedicating yourselves to serving the people, you will be tested by patients and work. You should encourage each other even more. Li said, "If it weren't for the great power of nursing care, I might have left this world long ago and wouldn't be able to gather with you all." Finally, he gave four pieces of advice: don't be afraid of hard work, be thorough and rigorous in your work, treat patients with the utmost love, and enhance the status and personality of nurses. Li mentioned in his speech that his niece is currently studying nursing at the Central Hospital in the capital and will soon graduate.

Two Songs - Everyone present was moved by Mr. Li's words, and applause thundered for a while. Then, students from Qingxin Girls' High School sang two famous songs, "Spring" and "River of Minadong," which were melodious and pleasant, captivating the listeners. The whole place was filled with a pure and lively atmosphere. Head Nurse Miss Xie Po thanked the guests in the lingering sound and encouraged the graduates with the three words: Faith, Hope, and Love.

Nurse Nominations - Finally, Mrs. Li presented the certificates, representatives of male and female students expressed their gratitude, and Pastor You Shuxun prayed, and the ceremony ended. Four major foreign oil companies in the city, Mobil, Asiatic Petroleum, Texaco, and 油遍地, have reduced the retail prices of kerosene and gasoline due to the sluggish market and weak purchasing power. The details are as follows:

Kerosene Prices Reduced Across the Board by Thirty Cents

According to kerosene industry insiders, the British, American, and Russian oil companies in the city have reduced prices to maintain their Chinese market share. The price of kerosene has been reduced from $8.50 to $8.20 per ten gallons, a decrease of thirty cents. Gasoline Prices Also Fall

Gasoline prices also fell yesterday. Loose gasoline is now sold at 87 cents per gallon, barrel gasoline with the empty barrel returned is sold at 90 cents per gallon, and canned gasoline is sold at 93 cents per gallon, an average decrease of four cents compared to the previous price. Further increases or decreases will be considered based on market demand.
