Nanyang Islands: Decline in Sales of National Porcelain Due to Dumping of Japanese Porcelain 129

According to the International Trade Bureau yesterday, the products exported from our country to the Nanyang Islands for sale are mainly tea, red tobacco, and groceries. Porcelain also has a fairly large annual import volume to the Nanyang Islands. However, in recent years, the porcelain from Jiangxi, Dehua, and Shantou, which used to sell for millions of dollars in the Southern Islands, has also been greatly affected, and business has plummeted. The biggest reason is the competition and dumping of Japanese porcelain. It is found that Japanese porcelain already accounts for 80-90% of the various porcelain shops in Nanyang. Japanese porcelain is not only less than half the price of products from our country, but even the styles and shapes are similar to our products. Therefore, national porcelain is almost at the end of its strength in Nanyang. It is found that most of those engaged in the porcelain industry are from Fujian and Chaozhou. There are two sources of porcelain: Jiangxi products, mostly fine porcelain, and some porcelain products similar to antiques, such as porcelain Buddhas, vases, and stove bricks. Products from Shantou and Dehua are mostly coarse porcelain, such as bowls, plates, jars, and cups. With the recent import and sale of Japanese porcelain to the Nanyang Islands, all kinds of supplies are available. At first, the colors, styles, and shapes were easily distinguishable, but recent products are difficult to distinguish. Unless one is experienced in the industry, it is not easy to immediately distinguish the origin of the goods. According to people in the industry, the method of identifying porcelain can be simply divided into two categories: first, by form and use; second, by material. Regarding the first, there are several points: First, the form and painting of Japanese porcelain are quite artistic. The brushstrokes are close to the new style, and the colors are rich and bright. Among our country's products, the painting of Jiangxi porcelain can be considered exquisite, but the painting is fine, and the color tone is ultimately not as bright as Japanese goods. Shantou products are even inferior to Jiangxi porcelain. Second, the shapes of Japanese porcelain are mostly similar. Products from Shantou and Dehua often have uneven forms. Third, Japanese porcelain has very fast heat transfer. When filled with hot water or boiling soup, it often feels hot to the touch. Jiangxi products, because of the tight material structure, transfer heat more slowly. Shantou porcelain is the same. The second category is material, and there are also several points: First, Japanese porcelain is very light in weight. Jiangxi and Shantou porcelain are very heavy in weight. Second, the material of Jiangxi and Shantou products cannot be purely white, and the reflected light is quite strong. Third, when dissecting Jiangxi, Shantou, and Dehua porcelain, the material inside is dense and solid, while the material structure of Japanese porcelain is looser and has fine pores like slight fermentation, which is why it is so light in weight. If we pay attention to the above situation, we can surely tell the origin of the porcelain at a glance.

Young Woman Robbed and Shot to Death; Female Companion Describes the Incident; Insists a Robber Caused the Tragedy; Female Companion Says She Was Almost Involved 130

Cheng Cuiying, a young woman from Zhenjiang, living at No. 3 Shoufuli, Rongshi Road, Taiping Bridge, French Concession, accompanied by her younger sister Xu Xiuzhen, was walking west of Chenshi'an Bridge, Fangbang Road, at around noon the day before yesterday when two robbers suddenly caught up and forcibly grabbed the gold bracelet on Cuiying's arm. Because she resisted, she was shot in the head by the robber and fell to the ground. The robbers succeeded and fled without a trace. After the police station in charge sent Cheng Cuiying to Shanghai Hospital for treatment, she died on the way. These details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now learned that yesterday morning, Jiang Pingyang, the head of the ninth district, filed a report with the Shanghai Local Court with the young woman Xu Xiuzhen, requesting an autopsy. According to Xu Xiuzhen, a native of Zhenjiang, 22 years old, residing at No. 7 Lanxinli, Bair Road, she and the deceased Cheng Cuiying were close friends. Recently, because Cuiying intended to go to Xiaodongmen to buy foreign cloth, she had come to my house several times and asked me to accompany her. Because my newborn baby was only two months old and had been unwell recently, my mother repeatedly refused to let me go with her. Cuiying left unhappily upon hearing this. Yesterday morning at 11 a.m., Cuiying came to my house again and invited me to go buy cloth together. Because my mother had repeatedly prevented me and the child was slightly better, I held the child and went out with her. Initially, we intended to go to Xiaodongmen to buy foreign cloth, but when we reached the east end of the City God Temple, Cuiying suddenly said she would buy it another day, so we turned back west. When we reached the entrance of the City God Temple, Cuiying invited me to eat sweet fermented rice balls inside the gate. Because it was almost noon, I thought this kind of waste could be saved, and Cuiying agreed, so we walked home slowly, talking as we went. When we reached the west end of Chenshi'an Bridge, robbers suddenly caught up and robbed Cuiying's gold bracelet (two silk strands, worth eighty yuan). Cuiying refused to let go and struggled with them. Suddenly, I heard a gunshot from behind. I immediately told Cuiying to let go, but she stubbornly grabbed one of the robbers and refused to release him. Just as things were at a critical moment, I heard another gunshot, and I saw Cuiying fall to the ground. The bullet grazed my ear. At first, I didn't realize Cuiying was injured, so I went forward to help her up. In an instant, I saw blood flowing from Cuiying's forehead, and she was unconscious. I was shocked and quickly hired a car with the two children (one was Cuiying's two-year-old child, Ailin) and went home to report. I was also almost involved, etc. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Li Fen, commissioned by the court, came with Examiner Xuan Zhiming to the court. It was confirmed that the deceased Cheng Cuiying died from a bullet penetrating her brain. It was decided that the family would collect the body and wait for the arrest and punishment of the murderer.

Dispute Over Forcibly Pulling a Woman Outside the Court; Fallout from a Divorce Case; Woman Vows Not to Return Home 131

Wang Shanlu, a native of Ningbo who lives in Yongxinli, Geller Road, French Concession, and works as a cigarette peddler, married Wang Renjuan (28 years old this year), the daughter of his fellow villager Wang Jinzhang, through a matchmaker. After the marriage, the couple loved each other dearly and had a son who is now eight years old. Recently, Wang Renjuan, unable to bear her husband's abuse, left home with her son and filed a petition with the Civil Mediation Office of the Second Special Court, requesting mediation and divorce from her husband, Wang Shanlu. The court accepted the petition, and yesterday morning at around 10 a.m., Judge Li Liang specially opened Civil Court No. 7 for mediation. Both parties were summoned to court. First, the petitioner Wang Renjuan testified about the unbearable pain of cohabiting with her abusive husband and requested permission to divorce. When questioned, the opposing party Wang Shanlu testified that his wife went out on the fifth of this month and could not be found anywhere. He had reported it to the police and opposed the divorce, requesting that the petitioner be ordered to return home and live together. After examining the testimony, the court declared the mediation unsuccessful and ordered the petitioner to file a formal lawsuit separately, and ordered the two parties to go out and reconcile themselves, and then adjourned the court. When the two parties left the court, several male and female relatives of the man blocked the woman's way and ordered her to go home. Wang resolutely opposed and refused to go back. While the two sides were arguing, three or four young women on the woman's side hired a car and came to help, forcibly trying to take Wang away in the car. At this point, Wang Shanlu believed that these four women, whom he did not know, should not deliberately obstruct the reconciliation of the couple while their family was experiencing sorrow, and he could not help but be angry and stepped forward to question them. Wang's friends also helped to hold the three women. While they were arguing, the police arrived and took both parties to the Central Police Station. After questioning by the head of the police station, the case was dismissed as a family dispute. Wang walked out of the police station and, seeing that the road was full of her husband's relatives, fearing that she would be surrounded again, she ran to the Second Court's bailiff room to take refuge. After Judge Li, who was handling the case, learned about it, he reopened the court and ordered the bailiff to summon both parties to the case for questioning. What are you arguing about outside? Wang tearfully testified that she did not want to go home now and that they had forcibly blocked her. She was working as a hired hand at the Old Garbage Bridge and had a fixed address, so why must they force her to go home? The official then painstakingly persuaded both parties that reconciliation outside the court was advisable and summoned Wang Renjuan's father, Wang Gangzhang, to the court, ordering Wang to return home with her husband. If they wanted to beat her, the law would protect her, and they would certainly not make things difficult for her in the same way. He then ordered Wang Shanlu's side to wait for a moment and ordered Wang to leave the court with her father first and go home with peace of mind. About a quarter of an hour later, Wang Shanlu was ordered to leave the court and return home. A humorous scene of forcibly pulling and entanglement arising from a divorce case came to an end.

Yong'an Silver Company Case: Several Households Have Reached a Settlement; Luo Meifang Acquitted After Interrogation; Lin Kanghou Again Fails to Attend Meeting 132

The Yong'an Silver Company, which has been bankrupt for half a year, has not yet found a way to pay off its debts, leading to accusations of fraud and embezzlement against the company's directors, general manager, deputy manager, Deng Jing, Li Du, Wang Jiazhen, Mo Dehui, Lin Kanghou, Qian Youju, Ye Hanshui, Zhang Zilian, Peng Baohui, Lin Qiuhu, Gu Chuntao, Jiang Qi, Dai Kechang, Ou Jiancheng, Shen Zufu, Wang Shuixin, Luo Huafang, and other seventeen people. The number of lawsuits has increased to thirteen. Of the defendants, only Ou and Luo had previously been summoned to court, and Ou was ordered to pay 30,000 yuan and Luo 5,000 yuan as bail pending trial, as reported in the newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Zehan opened the court for further trial. Only one defendant, Luo Huafang, and his defense lawyer, Chen Tingrui, reported to the court. The rest failed to attend despite being summoned. Ou Jiancheng's defense lawyer, Li Shirui, gave a detailed report on the recent situation of negotiation and settlement between the two parties regarding the valuation of debts, requesting a further postponement, and stated that the valuation of the four households including Peng Zican and the Li Liangbin household had been settled out of court. The plaintiff's lawyers in the two cases then requested to withdraw the lawsuits, and the court approved the request. Other plaintiffs requested to withdraw the portion of the lawsuit against Lin Kanghou, and some requested to withdraw the portions of the lawsuit against Mo Dehui and Jiang Qi. The court approved these requests separately. However, lawyer Chen Tingrui requested that the portion of the lawsuit against Luo Huafang be tried first, stating that Luo only served as deputy manager after the company resumed business, and the cases filed by the plaintiffs had nothing to do with Luo. However, Luo still attended every hearing and was ordered to pay bail, which was very painful if prolonged. Therefore, he requested that all cases with Luo's name as a defendant be investigated first. Lin Kanghou's lawyer still stated that Lin was unable to attend due to attending a meeting. Judge Wu then declared that there were currently thirteen lawsuits against Yong'an for unpaid debts. Except for the self-accusers who requested a full withdrawal of their lawsuit, there were still nine cases. Of these, only the lawsuit filed by Chen Shengyao and other five households listed the defendant Luo Huafang's name. After questioning the self-accuser Feng Shunji and others in the newly filed lawsuit about the facts of the accusation, the relationship between Luo and the lawsuit would be studied, and Lin Kanghou's lawyer would be told that Lin Kanghou's excuse of attending a meeting every time he was summoned was an intentional evasion, and that if he failed to attend again, he would be dealt with according to the law. After the declaration, the nature of the debts owed to Feng Shunji was investigated. Lawyer Li stated that the money handed over to the company by Feng was a deposit, which was different from other deposits, and that he still owed the company debts and had now filed a lawsuit against Feng, and that it was still difficult to determine who the creditor was. Judge Wu then inquired of Luo Huafang and determined that Luo had no suspicion of embezzlement or fraud and had no relationship with the deposits of Chen Shengyao and others, and immediately announced that Luo Huafang was found not guilty. The remaining cases were adjourned for further trial.

Miserable Death of Apprentice Plasterer Subject to Autopsy 139

Yuan Linsheng, a male child from Nantong, seventeen years old this year, whose parents died early, was brought to Shanghai by his adoptive father Wu Lianfa (34 years old this year) at the age of eleven. Through an introduction, he went to Chen Changsheng, a native of Pudong, who lived in a flat house in the west end of Xinyi Jia, Lujia Lane, Xujiahui Road, French Concession, to learn plastering apprenticeship, which is now about to be completed. Yesterday, a report was made to the Second Special District Court Procuratorate, and Chief Prosecutor Chen Bei and forensic recorders arrived at the station at noon to examine the body. It was confirmed that the deceased had died from injuries sustained in the fall during his lifetime. The investigation was opened, and the official questioned the family members about the incident. Origin of Firearms and Military Uniforms Stored in Southeast Medical College - Guo Qiyuan Clarifies Origins - Detective Team Postpones Investigation 142

Sha Daxin, the leader of the Detective Team of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, recently learned that a large number of firearms were hidden in military camps in the southern city. Yesterday morning at around six o'clock, he, along with Deputy Team Leader Wang Fu, supervised detectives Yuan Zhigang, Li Faxiang, Shi Yongquan, etc., and together with Inspector Guo of the Dongjiadu Police Station, went to the address for a search. In a small room on the third floor of the college, they found five rifles and eight hundred grey military uniforms. They immediately arrested the college's general affairs officer Li Yunmen (49 years old, from Jiangyin), the tea boy Kai Yi (44 years old, from Beiping), and Yao Yusheng (25 years old, from Jiangyin), and took them back to the team. Later, around eight o'clock, Team Leader Sha and the head of the Ximen Branch Bureau rushed to the home of Guo Qiyuan, president of the Southeast Medical College and Southeast Hospital at No. 8 Taiheng Lane, Zhonghua Road, Ximen. They found a Browning pistol, a gun license, a Mauser pistol, and more than forty bullets. Guo happened to be at home and was immediately detained and taken back to the team along with the evidence. During the preliminary hearing proposed by General Team Leader Lu, Guo Qiyuan stated that he was 37 years old and from Jiangyin. During the January 28th Shanghai Incident, he served as the leader of the 7th team of the Chinese Red Cross Rescue Team. Later, after the 19th Route Army retreated to the second line of defense, He Xiangning and others, a commissioner, established the National Disaster Relief Team and Rear Hospital in Suzhou. I then merged with the hospital and simultaneously served as the director of the hospital. The Browning pistol and Mauser pistol found at my home by the detectives this time were both prepared for self-defense by myself. The pistol has a license, and the Mauser pistol is in the process of getting a new license. As for the five rifles stored in the college, they were picked up from the battlefield before. The eight hundred military uniforms were left over from purchases for the wounded and sick in the hospital and were kept in the college for poor patients to change into. Because the matter was important, he was ordered to leave it to the staff for verification.

Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau - Bans Inferior Proprietary Medicines - Promulgates Rules for Registration of Proprietary Medicines 150

The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, in order to ban inferior proprietary medicines and maintain the health of citizens, has specially formulated the Shanghai Municipal Rules for the Registration of Proprietary Medicines in accordance with the Central Government's promulgated rules for the administration of proprietary medicines, so as to provide a basis for handling registration matters. The rules have been approved and promulgated by the Municipal Government, and the Health Bureau has ordered all pharmacies in the city to comply with them. The announcement and rules are extracted below:

Announcement. It is noted that there are many kinds of proprietary medicines sold in this city. In order to prevent malpractices and maintain the health of citizens, this Bureau has specially formulated 10 items of the Shanghai Municipal Rules for the Registration of Proprietary Medicines in accordance with the provisions of Article 4 of the Ministry of Interior's Rules for the Administration of Proprietary Medicines, which have been submitted to the Municipal Government under Directive No. 14015 for approval and promulgation. In addition to registration today, the full text of the rules is attached below for each pharmacist to follow.

Rules. (1) These rules are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 4 of the Ministry of Interior's Rules for the Administration of Proprietary Medicines. (2) Anyone who manufactures, imports, or sells proprietary medicines within this city's district shall comply with these rules in addition to complying with the rules for the administration of proprietary medicines. (3) After each type of proprietary medicine has been submitted to the Ministry of Interior for inspection and has been found qualified and a license has been issued, it should be immediately submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau for registration. (4) When applying for registration, in addition to filling out an application form for each type of proprietary medicine, the following items should also be submitted: 1. A proprietary medicine permit issued by the Ministry. 2. Samples. 3. A registration license fee of 2 yuan and a stamp duty fee of 1 yuan. Registration will be approved only after review and approval. Proprietary medicines that have been inspected and qualified by the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau's Hygiene Laboratory before obtaining the Ministry's permit may be exempted from the registration license fee, but the stamp duty fee must still be paid. (5) Any type of proprietary medicine that does not have a permit will not be registered, and it shall not be sold within this city's district unless it has been approved for registration. (6) If a registration license is damaged or lost, it may be reissued upon payment of a stamp duty fee. (7) The advertisements, leaflets, and grades attached to the containers and packaging paper of all proprietary medicines shall comply with the provisions of Articles 9 to 12 of the Rules for the Administration of Proprietary Medicines, and shall not use words such as "Health Bureau Guarantee" [blank space]. (8) Violations of these rules shall be punished in accordance with the provisions of the Rules for the Administration of Proprietary Medicines. (9) If there are any unsuitable matters in these rules, they may be amended at any time. (10) These rules shall be implemented from the date of submission for approval.

Therefore, anyone who experiences side effects from taking baking soda or cannot tolerate baking soda should use Alucol. This medicine is very easy to digest and convenient to take. No matter what kind of stomach ailment is being treated, it can prevent the ailment from recurring. It is truly an essential item for every household. Educational News

Siam Intensifies the Destruction of Overseas Chinese Education: Newly Issued Mandatory Class Schedules and Orders for Chinese Schools to Re-register; Plans to Merge All Chinese Schools and Force School-Age Overseas Chinese Children to Attend 156

(Bangkok Airmail) The Siamese government is implementing a policy of assimilation towards overseas Chinese. It has scheduled the abolition of mandatory classes in Chinese schools on April 1st of this year, ordering overseas Chinese children to attend Siamese schools to receive their assimilation education. Details have been provided in previous communications. Since this event, the overseas Chinese in Siam have generally recognized that the Siamese government's policy of assimilating our overseas Chinese is poisonous and must be opposed to the death. Therefore, they have both telegraphed the central government, requesting active negotiations, and sent representatives back to the country to present their case and urge action. At the same time, they are seeking local solutions, requesting the Siamese authorities to temporarily maintain the status quo while our government formally negotiates with Siam, cancels all previous harsh regulations, and preserves the freedom of our overseas Chinese education. Simultaneously, compatriots in the country have also risen to support them. The Guangdong Miscellaneous Grain Adjustment Committee has even proposed banning the import of Siamese rice to prompt the Siamese side to realize the situation. This news reached Siam at the end of March, causing a brief period of panic among the Siamese authorities. The State Council immediately resolved to withdraw the order to abolish mandatory classes in Chinese schools. However, at that time, only a phone call was made to Mr. Ma Liqun, the acting chairman of the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce (the chairman, Chen Shouming, is currently on leave from Siam), and no formal order was delivered. Subsequently, due to the Education Minister, Phraya Phison Saraphaphan, being strong and unwilling to withdraw the order (the previous order to abolish mandatory classes in Chinese schools was issued by the Ministry of Education), and because the news of our country banning Siamese rice was only a flash in the pan for the authorities and was not actually implemented, the matter of withdrawing the order was shelved. A few days later, the Ministry of Education publicly announced newly revised mandatory class schedules, with 23 hours of Siamese language per week, increasing the school hours by one hour and forty-five minutes, while the time for Chinese language was not included in the curriculum. It also ordered all schools that wanted to run mandatory classes to re-register, and only those approved by the Ministry of Education would be allowed to enroll students of mandatory age. Thus, the power of deprivation still rests with the Ministry of Education. The newly revised curriculum for private schools (referring to Chinese schools) running mandatory classes is listed below:

Grade 1 Grade 2 Grade 3 Grade 4 Grade 5

Moral Education 1.00 1.30 1.00 1.00 1.00

Siamese 12.30 11.00 10.00 8.00 3.00

Arithmetic 5.00 5.00 4.00 3.00 2.00

General Knowledge 2.30 3.30 5.00 7.00 10.00

Hygiene 1.00 1.00 1.00 1.00 1.00

Drawing 1.00 1.00

Scouting 1.00 1.00 1.00 1.00 1.00

Crafts or Commerce 1.00 1.00 1.00 (Note: The above curriculum requires 23 hours of instruction per week, all of which must be taught in Siamese.) Since the announcement of the newly revised curriculum, all Chinese schools have recognized that the Ministry of Education's policy is a retreat in disguise. Nominally, it allows Chinese schools to continue running mandatory classes, but in reality, it increases the time for Siamese language and restricts Chinese schools from freely operating. Therefore, representatives of these mandatory classes have repeatedly visited the Education Minister to request a flexible solution. However, the Education Minister's attitude is strong and unyielding, with no room for compromise. Finally, he explicitly stated to the authorities of the Chinese schools that the Chinese schools must merge and no longer be established separately as before. After the merger, if they can be affiliated with the Ministry of Education and operate in accordance with the educational goals and national policies of the Siamese government, the Ministry of Education will provide the schools with economic subsidies. The representatives and principals of the Chinese schools, knowing the intention behind this statement, expressed their agreement on the spot. Afterwards, because it was during the vacation period, re-registration was not carried out. The Siamese government then took the opportunity to implement the second step of its strategy, issuing a notice through the county offices, ordering children subject to mandatory education to attend nearby Siamese schools starting May 1st, because Chinese schools have not yet re-registered with the Ministry of Education to become mandatory schools and therefore have no right to enroll students of mandatory age. Currently, the authorities of the Chinese schools and parents are hoping that our government will actively take effective measures to protest to the Siamese side, cancel all harsh regulations. If there is any further delay, all overseas Chinese children will be forced to attend Siamese schools and receive their assimilation education. As a reporter looking north, I implore the authorities and compatriots across the country on behalf of the three million overseas Chinese to lend a helping hand quickly.

Ministry of Education Clarifies Doubts Regarding the Graduation Examination Regulations for Middle School and Normal School Students 158

The Ministry of Education issued a notice to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities on the 13th, stating: "According to the request from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education to interpret doubts regarding the graduation examination regulations for middle school and normal school students, the following explanations are provided: (1) For junior high school students who have not undergone the joint examination or spot check and still take the graduation examination held by the school, their graduation certificates will only be stamped and state that 'Approved by the Ministry of Education to be exempted from the joint examination, and passed the school examination with passing grades.'

(2) Students who fail one or two subjects in the graduation joint examination are allowed to participate in the joint examination for those subjects twice in the next two sessions. That is, they have a total of three opportunities to take the exam, and it should not be difficult to pass. If they still fail, if they are directly required to repeat the grade in accordance with the rule for failing three or more subjects, it will cause those who have already applied for further education to drop out midway and re-enter junior high school or senior high school, creating various difficulties. If they are directly issued a certificate of completion in accordance with the method for those who cannot repeat the grade for certain reasons, it will also cause those who have already gone on to further education to lose their student status. If they are allowed to participate in the joint examination for the failed subjects indefinitely, it will also be unreasonable. The compromise solution is to hold a full examination, which still implies relief within the restrictions.

(3) If a student is absent from the joint examination due to a legitimate reason, the lack of grades for the missing subject is no different from failing one or two subjects in the joint examination. Therefore, they are also allowed to continue to participate in the joint examination twice in the next two sessions to avoid disputes and ensure uniformity. Since the missing subject is considered a failure and must be retaken, there is no need to use the usual grades as the grade for that subject. As for the absence from all subjects due to a legitimate reason, it is different from failing three or more subjects in the joint examination. There is no need to repeat the grade and they are allowed to continue to participate in the joint examination twice in the next two sessions, but such students are allowed to repeat the grade if they wish.

(4) Allowing students who fail one or two subjects in the joint examination to apply for further education in advance is to provide convenience for those going on to further education. However, only after they have passed all the subjects in the joint examination and obtained a junior high school or senior high school graduation certificate can they participate in the graduation examination of the school they have entered. This emphasizes the foundation of academic studies and strictly regulates admission qualifications. It is impossible to relax the rules later because of the leniency given earlier. In fact, if the grades in the years after entering further education are all passing, the subjects that fail in one or two subjects will not fail three times in a row. If they still fail, they can only participate in the joint examination for all subjects. If the study period in the school they have entered has expired and the grades over the years are all passing, then the graduation examination of the student in that school can be retained, and they can participate in the graduation examination of that school after obtaining the qualification for junior high school or senior high school graduation.

(5) The certificate of passing the graduation joint examination and the certificate of applying for further education should both have the student's photo affixed and stamped with the seal of the competent educational administrative authority. After the graduation certificate is issued or they go on to further education, they should be revoked as planned. In addition to the separate orders, the above explanations are hereby recorded and a copy of the original submission from the Jiangsu Education Department is attached for your information." This order includes a copy of the original submission from the Jiangsu Education Department requesting an explanation of the doubts regarding the graduation joint examination regulations for middle school and normal school students.

Copy of the original submission: Received the instructions from your ministry, No. 4266, to abolish the school graduation examination for middle schools and normal schools, and to issue revised graduation joint examination regulations for middle school and normal school students, which should be followed. After carefully examining the revised regulations, there are still several doubts that need to be clarified:

1. Article 9 of the Revised Middle School Graduation Joint Examination Regulations stipulates that all subjects in the graduation joint examination must be passed before graduation, and the graduation certificate will be issued by the school after being stamped by the educational administrative organs of the provinces and cities and affixed with the graduation joint examination mark. Students who pass the joint examination or spot check have no problem, but for junior high school students who have not undergone the spot check and still take the graduation examination held by the school, it seems inappropriate to affix the same mark if the graduation certificate is also affixed with the mark, otherwise there is an obvious distinction. How should this be handled? This is the first point that needs to be clarified.

2. Article 11 of the Revised Middle School and Normal School Graduation Joint Examination Regulations stipulates that students who fail one or two subjects in the joint examination are allowed to continue to participate in the joint examination for those subjects twice in the next two sessions before they can graduate. If they still fail in any subject, they should take the joint examination for all subjects. The original intention of the legislation was to allow students who fail one or two subjects to continue to participate in the joint examination for those subjects twice in the next two sessions, precisely to give them a chance to succeed. However, if there are still subjects that fail, it is not appropriate to deny the recognition of all the subjects that have already been passed and to retake all the examinations. This is not only too strict, but also difficult to implement in practice. It seems that the method in Article 10 should be followed. If there are still subjects that fail in the second joint examination, the original school should issue a certificate of completion, stating the grades of all subjects in the graduation joint examination, and affixing a mark indicating that a certain subject in the graduation joint examination failed twice. This is the second point that needs to be clarified. 3. Article 11, paragraph 2, of the Revised Middle School and Normal School Graduation Joint Examination Regulations stipulates that those who are unable to take all or part of the required subjects in the joint examination due to certain reasons will have their missing subjects marked as failing. This is also to prevent students from temporarily evading the examination and to strictly limit it. However, some participating students may have asked for leave in advance due to illness or important matters, and will participate in the joint examination in the next session. Others may have suddenly become ill during the examination, or may not be able to attend the examination for one or more subjects. These students should not be treated as failing in all cases. The circumstances should be considered, the facts should be investigated, and they should be allowed to take a makeup examination in the next session. Those who fail to take the examination without a valid reason or violate the rules of the examination hall should be marked as failing. In addition, if a missing subject is marked as failing, the grade is of course invalid. Should the usual grade, i.e. one-fourth, be used as the grade for that subject? If all subjects are missing and marked as failing, should they be made to repeat the grade, or is it unnecessary to repeat the grade, and they are allowed to participate in the joint examination in the next session? This is the third point that needs to be clarified.

4. Article 12 of the Revised Middle School Graduation Joint Examination Regulations stipulates that students who fail one or more subjects in the joint examination are allowed to apply for further education in advance. If they are admitted, they will be treated as probationary students, and only after they have passed the joint examination for those subjects and obtained a graduation certificate can they participate in the graduation examination of the school they have entered. This restriction will inevitably cause difficulties in the future when the students are handling graduation at the schools they have entered. For example, if the students participate in the joint examination for those subjects twice and still have failing subjects, but their grades in the school they have entered are all passing over the years, it seems inappropriate to cancel their graduation examination for this reason, as it does not encourage students to make progress and has a great impact that cannot be ignored. This is the fourth point that needs to be clarified.

5. Article 14 of the Revised Middle School and Normal School Graduation Joint Examination Regulations stipulates that students who pass the joint examination will first be issued a certificate of passing the graduation joint examination, and Article 11 of the Middle School Joint Examination Regulations stipulates that students who fail one or two subjects will be issued a certificate of applying for further education. This is to facilitate students' further education and service. However, in addition to the certificate, a graduation certificate must still be issued in the future. To prevent abuses, it seems that when the graduation certificate is issued, the original school should be held responsible for recovering the certificate of passing and submitting it to the competent educational administrative authority for cancellation. The certificate of applying for further education should be recovered by the school they have entered and submitted to the original issuing competent educational administrative authority for cancellation to prevent others from impersonating them. Furthermore, the certificate of applying for further education can only be used as proof of applying for further education and cannot be used for other purposes. This is the fifth point that needs to be clarified. The above points concern the ambiguities of the articles. Therefore, this document is submitted to request your review and prompt instructions. Respectfully presented to Wang, Minister of Education, Zhou Fohai, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, April 18, 24th year. The Industrial Federation and the China Association Host a Banquet

Excellent Chinese Engineering Students Returning from Internships in London: The Industrial Federation and the China Association Host a Banquet 159

(London, Havana, 13th) The Industrial Federation and the China Association jointly sponsored excellent Chinese engineering students for an internship of one and a half years in British factories. The first batch of two students, namely Zhu Changye (transliteration), who interned in electrical engineering, and Zhang Haitao (transliteration), who interned in locomotive manufacturing, have completed their terms and are about to return to the country to serve. The Industrial Federation and the China Association recently hosted a banquet to bid them farewell. Lieutenant General McDonough, Chairman, delivered a speech, saying, "Chinese students coming here for internships may not see immediate results, but it is hoped that after they learn the British modern mechanical standards and methods, they will return to the country to serve. With their reputation growing day by day, it will increase the opportunity for British industry to participate in China's economic development." The second batch of six Chinese internship students arrived in England last month, and three more will come here in June of this year. From 1934 to 1935, there were a total of sixteen people, which is far from the number desired by British factories.

Zhang Yuanruo Lectures at Tongji University: Self-Reliance and Diligent Service 161

The Affiliated Senior Vocational School of Tongji University in Jiangwan yesterday invited Zhang Yuanruo to give a lecture entitled "Self-Reliance and Diligent Service." Mr. Zhang elaborated in detail on his recently created self-reliance doctrine, extensively citing historical facts from China and abroad, and drawing on the theories of various scholars. His words were insightful and inspiring. He briefly stated that self-reliance is the antithesis of liberalism, and must be based on obligations and responsibilities, aimed at society and the country, and seeking the completion of self-personality. Therefore, the worldview of self-reliance advocates should be based on labor service as the goal. This also has its basis in philosophy. All the wise emperors and virtuous ministers of the past who were able to achieve great things for the country had this spirit. Extending this to the survival of the universe, the life of the nation, the evolution of society, and the development of culture, all are due to labor service. China's past education was decadent and nihilistic, the national spirit was weak and demoralized, real talents and practical learning were not developed, and the inherent cultural creative ability of the Chinese nation gradually disappeared, leading to national poverty, economic decline, and national decline to this extreme. Therefore, the most practical way to save the country today is to first base it on the principle of self-reliance, to inspire the national enthusiasm and vitality for saving and building the country, and those in power should also take the spirit of diligence and national revival of Dayu and the Duke of Zhou as an example for the people, encouraging each other from top to bottom, and working hard throughout the country, so that there is hope for revival. The reason why European countries were able to break free from their medieval dark ages and have today's civilization and prosperity is also due to the awakening of their national self and the efforts of their national self. This is a successful precedent of self-reliance, and it is also the most powerful factual explanation of self-reliance.

The District Investigation Committee has also been organized. The investigation committee members include Wang Dasui, Director of the Public Security Branch Bureau, Dong Pingyu, Director of the Police Station, Tu Tongfu, Head of the Security Corps, and representatives of each team leader, police station chief, and district branch, Ni Wenya, Director of Da Zhong University, and principals of various schools, totaling forty people. Wang Dasui, director of the District Investigation Committee, and Dong Pingyu, deputy director, convened the first meeting of all members in the headquarters of the Pu Song Town Security Corps on the morning of the 12th to promote the work. It was resolved that the district would be divided into ten districts with reference to the jurisdiction of the police districts, and the investigators would be divided into ten groups, with one group leader and ten members in each group. Each district would cooperate and carry out the work simultaneously. Currently, the candidates for group leaders and members have been separately appointed, and the investigation work will begin as soon as the teachers sent by the General Office arrive.

National Sports Association Calls for a Sports Discussion - Late July and Early August in Qingdao - Outline and Schedule Already Arranged 170

The All-China Sports Federation, in order to gather sports experts from all over the country in one place to jointly conduct academic discussions on various sports issues in the country, so as to improve and implement plans, has decided to hold a sports discussion meeting at Shandong University in Qingdao from July 29th to August 3rd this year. The outline of the measures has been formulated as follows:

Outline of Measures Article 1. This association will hold a discussion meeting at Shandong University in Qingdao from July 29th to August 3rd this year to gather sports experts from all over the country for academic discussions on various sports issues in the country. Article 2. In addition to the general meeting, this discussion meeting will be divided into the following four groups: (1) Sports Administration Group, (2) University Sports Group, (3) Middle School Sports Group, (4) Mass Sports Group. Article 3. The methods of discussion for this discussion meeting are stipulated as follows: (1) The president of this association (Federation) will chair the general meeting. (2) Each group will be chaired by a person designated by this association, and the chairman will designate a recorder from among those present. (3) Each group will propose several questions by this association, and experts will be requested to prepare papers in advance and read them at the meeting. (4) After each paper is read, all those present may participate in the discussion of the paper. (5) Each group will elect several sorting committee members before the closing meeting to sort out the papers and discussion results and put forward concrete suggestions for reference by the national sports community. Article 4. Members participating in the discussion meeting will be provided with accommodation by this association in Qingdao during the meeting period, and other expenses will be borne by themselves. Article 5. Those who wish to participate in this discussion meeting are requested to notify the Preparatory Office of this association at Shandong University in Qingdao by letter five days before the meeting, and report to this association when they arrive at the meeting. Article 6. The schedule of the discussion meeting will be determined separately. Article 7. These measures shall be implemented upon approval by the Standing Committee of Directors of this association.

Discussion Schedule Day 1 (July 29th) Noon, General Meeting: 1. Opening Ceremony, 2. Chairman's Opening Speech, 3. Secretary-General's Report on Preparations, 4. Speech: The Goals of Sports in China, 5. Photography. Day 2 (July 30th) Noon, Administration Group: 1. Prospects for Sports Administration in China, 2. Suggestions for the Sports Administration System in China, 3. Review of the Training of Sports Talents in China, 4. Sports Administration for Women in China. Day 3 (July 31st) Noon, University Group: 1. Discussion on University Sports Facilities, 2. Methods for Promoting University Intra-School Competitions, 3. Principles and Methods for University Inter-School Competitions. Day 4 (August 1st) Noon, Middle School Group: 1. Discussion on Middle School Sports Teaching Materials, 2. Organization and Methods for Middle School Sports Extracurricular Activities, 3. The Interrelationship between Sports, Military Training, and Boy Scouts in the Middle School Curriculum. Day 5 (August 2nd) Noon, Mass Group: 1. Principles for Promoting Mass Sports, 2. Management of Sports Fields, 3. Discussion on Mass Sports Teaching Materials, 4. Mass Sports and Mass Education. Day 6 (August 3rd) Noon, General Meeting: 1. Reports from the Sorting Committee of Each Group, 2. Chairman's Closing Speech, 3. Miscellaneous Motions and Discussions.

Public Lectures: 1. Zhang Boling will talk about Chinese sports from the perspective of education, 2. Shen Siliang will talk about China's international sports, 3. Zhang Jiwu will talk about the latest sports situation in Europe and the United States. Dates to be determined.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 173

— (Microorganism)

Ink, everyone knows it's black. There's an old saying, "One who stays near vermilion gets stained red, and one who stays near ink gets stained black." The red ink and blue ink used in schools clearly don't have a trace of black in them. I wonder where the ink is in them?

The towels used in bathhouses don't distinguish between top and bottom. The bathhouse attendant sometimes "wipes people's feet and buttocks," and sometimes "wipes people's hands and faces." It's just like people drinking wine only waiting for the wine to taste as sweet as honey in their mouths. They argue endlessly without considering the winemakers who at that time, with their bare black feet, climbed into the vat to "tread the yeast and mash," with "foot dirt" mixed in. This is probably holding on to the philosophy of "what the eye doesn't see, the heart doesn't grieve"!

The thing for brushing teeth is called a toothbrush, because it can brush away the dirt on the teeth. A scrubbing brush is used for brushing clothes. Logically, it should be called a "clothes brush," but it's called a scrubbing brush. Does that mean "clothes are wooden boards"?

Vinegar 174

— Lan Shan

Opening the door to seven things, "vinegar" is also one of them. When women sometimes crave sourness, use a little vinegar to prepare dishes, or buy some sour plums or pickled vegetables to eat as snacks, it's a sign of pregnancy. The whole family is overjoyed, playfully joking with her.

Hangzhou restaurants' vinegar-braised fish is well-known and popular, entirely dependent on the head of vinegar.

Women usually like to eat vinegar, the reason being, of course, for that sour taste, eating it brings a subtle feeling that can stimulate the stomach. So, people with stomach problems shouldn't eat sour and spicy foods. Not only do they eat vinegar, but at certain times, they are also skilled at making vinegar, capable of producing a very qualified product without the guidance of a vinegar master, that sour taste is enough to thoroughly fumigate their husbands. If Mr. So-and-so has a few encounters with Ms. So-and-so, and his wife sees it, she gets very angry. In this way, her raw material for making vinegar is also available, and she often uses those sour words to stimulate him. If he is willing to change his ways, that's all right. If he repeatedly refuses to reform, she overturns the vinegar vat and engages in a great battle with him. As a result, her acid reaction is often more powerful than a force of victory, easily conquering him!

Between husband and wife, sweetness is the principle. But going sweet all the way through is too cloying. Where is the excitement? Like side dishes, chicken, goose, fish, and meat are highly valued, but eating them for a long time gets tiring, and you have to change the pattern and change the taste. It's the same with husband and wife. Sometimes a little sour thing happens, adjusting each other's feelings and stimulating each other's appetite. This is harmless in general, as long as it's done in moderation, and not in excessive amounts. Otherwise, too much stimulation can lead to unfortunate accidents, turning it over, just like eating too much vinegar will cause nausea.

"Miscellaneous Records from the Garden of Leisure" has an interesting story about vinegar: "When Zhang Muan, the provincial administrator of Haifeng, went out one day, an old woman stopped his carriage to complain, saying that her husband had married a concubine and asked him to prohibit it. Zhang Gong laughed and sent her away, saying: 'I am an official who sells salt, and I don't care about people eating vinegar.'" Reading it can make you laugh out loud.

Old Man Yongchun 175

— Yu Qing

Old Woman Yongchun asked me to read a letter. As I read aloud the letter her son had sent, her two hollow eye sockets became somewhat watery. However, I was not moved in the slightest, as I was reminded of an ordinary man.

Old Man Yongchun was a quiet person who disliked activity, hence his face was stern and unchanging every day. Anyone who knew him, or had even seen him once, would say he had the look of a lonely old man.

He was the head of our clan, and I never heard anyone call him by his given name. Especially us younger members of the clan, we were obliged to call him "Grandpa," and seeing him was like a chick encountering a hawk, causing us to tremble with fear.

Every morning, he would get out of bed at the crack of dawn, and *duk, duk!* with a rhythmic beat, he would tap the floorboards with his long-stemmed pipe, which had become vermilion from sucking on it. The shop assistants sleeping in the store would hear his signal to get up, and they would hurriedly roll up their bedding.

Once the door panels were removed, the people of the town gradually gathered! The noise of voices grew clamorous! The broker strained his hoarse throat, shouting out the weight and market price of goods, busier than a broker in the stock exchange! Old Man Yongchun, as usual, would go to Ma Pingsheng's tea house at the east end of town for morning tea. He always brought his own small packet of "Yu Qian" (pre-Qingming tea). No one could stomach his tea, as it was even more bitter than medicine, but he would even chew the tea leaves and swallow them. When the market closed, he would bid farewell to his purple clay teapot with the coiled dragon design.

The reason I can still remember Old Man Yongchun is entirely due to the impression his moss-covered cakes left on me.

Eye-Brightening Lotion 176

— Juan Yin

Promote literacy education and eliminate illiteracy.

The Ethereal Record of Imperial Incense 177

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

"Form a circle!" After all the dogs had come out, he shouted this again; the dogs, upon hearing, all started running in circles in the open space in front, constantly barking, and their bright red tongues darted in and out. Several of the larger dogs even started doing somersaults on the spot, like a troop of mischievous elementary school students causing a ruckus on the playground. It looked truly innocent and lovely! Then, the eunuch shouted:

"Stop!" His shout was as effective as a command in the army. The dogs, upon hearing it, immediately calmed down and lined up in an orderly row, forming a line facing the row of attendants behind the Empress Dowager. Perhaps they stood even more orderly than we did! Their eyes were round and protruding, like two black chess pieces; at this moment, they were all staring at the Empress Dowager, staring without blinking, fully expressing the cleverness of trained domestic animals. However, if we only took a cursory glance, it would be difficult to see their eyes, because the tufts of hair on their heads were particularly long, so long that they covered their eyes. Only when the sunlight shone directly on their foreheads could we see those two lights, like small electric lights, flashing in the darkness. As for whether they had any difficulty seeing things, I cannot know.

By the time all the dogs had lined up in a straight line and were standing still, no longer jumping around, and their barking had also stopped, because their barking was not indiscriminate, the eunuch in charge of the dogs could make them bark when he wanted them to bark, and stop barking when he wanted them to stop. (314)

Biographical Sketches

Notes on Gao Zhifang (Part 2) 178

— Zhen Lü

He had participated in several long-distance races organized by the city government. Once, in a 20,000-meter race, he finished fifth out of nearly a hundred athletes, receiving some prizes from the authorities and a glorious record in the newspapers—the name Gao Zhifang briefly appeared in the sports world. Because I didn't know that this was A-Gen's name, I didn't pay attention. (He presented several old newspapers and medals he had kept as proof.) Although this did not help his difficult livelihood, and in fact consumed many days of earning money for preparation and practice, he himself was very satisfied.

Last year, he was admitted to the Shanghai Municipal Police Training Class, with Mr. Jiang Huaizhen acting as his guarantor. As usual, he studied for six months and graduated eighth out of over two hundred people, then was assigned to a police position in the Public Security Bureau, serving in the Sun Temple area of Zhabei. Relying on his conscience, based on what he had learned, he fulfilled his duties, but was envied by the local thugs and subjected to dishonorable accusations, almost leading to his dismissal. If it weren't for dozens of formal merchants jointly guaranteeing his character, even though the thugs eventually received a few months of detention by the court, he did not dare to compromise with the evil forces and secure his position, but still had to "go his own way," as he put it.

As for his motivation for joining the police force, it can also be explained. It turned out that one day, he pulled his empty rickshaw to the side of the road to rest, and was carefully counting his earnings when he glanced up and saw a tattered Party flag covering a pile of old utensils next to the gate of a wealthy family. A person, looking like a servant, was standing idly by the gate. He saw this and could no longer suppress his indignation. He walked over and, after confirming that the utensils belonged to the family, told the person that this was the hard-won emblem of the late Premier, which should be respected and not used carelessly, and asked him to put it away. The person initially ignored him, then said that he was just a rickshaw puller and not qualified to interfere, scolding him harshly. Seeing that his advice was ineffective, he invited a policeman to come and explained the situation to him, asking him to persuade the person. But the policeman also blamed him for meddling, and even threatened him. He was willing to go to the police station with the policeman and suffer the consequences, and of course he was subjected to minor physical punishments on the way. Fortunately, the officials in the station were wise and reprimanded the policeman. He had always been disgusted by the corruption and abuse of the working class by some policemen, and this incident further incited him, so he was determined to join the police force, hoping to lead by example. Now, he has indeed achieved his initial goal.

I see that this Gao Zhifang, although his knowledge is still shallow, is able to strive and move towards the right path. Therefore, at his sincere request, I write down some words to encourage him to make greater progress, and to show it to the general public of distressed young people.

Late-Night Tea 179

— Xin Ren

In the tea houses near the Wuxi train station, a large group of people go for late-night tea every night. These late-night tea drinkers are mostly those who have disembarked from fourth-class carriages. Most of them are victims of the market slump, leaving the city and returning to their baseless hometowns, hunched over, carrying their bundles of clothes. For the sake of a few cents of savings, braving the crowded fourth-class carriages, and to save a few coins on inn accommodations, they endure a sleepless night at the tea house. A pot of tea for sixteen coppers, three copper coins' worth of melon seeds, and a pungent dry tobacco pipe are their perfect late-night snack. They are just like the pleasure-seeking playboys in nightclubs, trying to while away the dark hours. Although some feel the night is too short, wishing time could grant them a few more moments, others curse the relentless continuation of the night, wishing they could break through the eastern sky and grab the bright sun.

The night continues relentlessly. Who really wants to drink late-night tea? So the late-night tea drinkers begin to yawn, and some inevitably strike up conversations with their neighbors.

"Are you going to Shanghai to work for someone?"

"Yes, the brokers' offices are so crowded that you can't squeeze in. I waited for several days, it's really not working out, so I had to come back."

They watch as the famine in the countryside drives them out, thinking of making a living in the city, but now they are squeezed out by the city. They talk with bitterness, ponder with bitterness, and drink bitter tea.

Most late-night tea drinkers are like this. Although they long for the sun to rise, they are still in darkness even when the sun comes out. Pungent tobacco pipes, bitter tea, and yawns come one after another.

Remembering West Lake 180

— (Shu Fan)

My horse's hooves lengthen as I ride south,

Lonely and desolate, Xiao Jiuniang near the lake.

I remember in years past, during the incense-burning festival,

I wagered and drank for her, busy the whole spring long.

The oars are blocked at Huang Xie Pier,

The setting sun slants by the Flower God Temple.

Every year I've been drunk for three months of spring,

But this year, I have no share in watching the falling flowers.

Long street, short trees, desolate at dusk,

Fireflies flit, busy continuously.

Not like gazing from Broken Bridge,

Drooping willows, disordered water, stars yellow.

Little Western Paradise 181

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 13: Difficult to be a Bridesmaid, Pitiful to Sell Oneself, Enslaved for Merchandise is Also Joyful, Bankruptcy Talks of Farm Life

Zhiqian looked around; the ground was swept clean, the bedding neatly folded, and there was nothing dirty. So he smiled and said: Beihai, we were just chatting in Mr. Zhou's room, never imagining there was someone here waiting for instructions. Beihai tugged at his collar, pressed his chest twice, then, clasping his books, smiled and entered. Because the corner of the table against which Yueying was pressing a garment was right in the path, Beihai still brushed past Yueying's side as he entered. As he walked past, Yueying turned her body slightly to let him pass. When he passed by, Beihai couldn't help but quickly glance at her face. Clearly, as he passed, the blush on her face seemed to deepen. And her head was lowered even more. Zhiqian looked at them both, then said to Beihai: I don't think we can study today, let's do it tomorrow. Beihai put his books on the table and then quickly moved to sit in a chair against the wall. In his heart, he was thinking, could it be that Mr. Cheng, so upright and generous, has some feelings for this young woman? I absolutely won't leave. That's what he was thinking, but he didn't say anything. Yueying, on the other hand, had another thought. It turned out that this young Mr. Wang came every day without fail. She had been holding the corner of the table, looking outwards. Thinking of this, she slowly turned half her body and quickly glanced at Beihai. Actually, even if she had really turned around and looked at Beihai face to face, Zhiqian wouldn't have minded much. It was just that her thinking about it and not daring to look openly told Zhiqian, who had long experience in the sea of people, that this was an expression of some mutual interest. In his heart, he thought, I'll keep quiet and see what happens with this young couple. (204)
