Free Talk

Who Puts the Focus of the Water Margin on Yun Prefecture? 198

— Linglu

Determining the location of Liangshan Marsh is probably helpful for those who enjoy studying the Water Margin, but it seems unnecessary to try to explain why Song Jiang would base himself there. I have always suspected whether Song Jiang and others ever permanently occupied Liangshan Marsh, but I have no interest in researching it. The simple reasons for my suspicion should be obvious and not worth publishing. However, since I have yet to see a similar and more insightful view, and some people are exploring in the opposite direction, my opinion might finally be worth mentioning.

According to various consistent references, the historical Song Jiang's bandit group originated in Hebei and was recruited into the imperial army in Haizhou. In between, they "rampaged through Qi and Wei," "attacked Huaiyang Military Prefecture," and "raided Jingdong." Thus, Song Jiang and his followers were clearly a band of roaming bandits. Their route was somewhat similar to that of Liu Hei Qi, who fled from Hebei back to Shandong the year before last. Although Song Jiang may not have covered such a long distance in the same short period, his life as a roaming bandit seems to have been just as short. The official histories do not record when Song Jiang started in Hebei, but the Stories of the Xuanhe Era records that Yang Zhi, Li Jinyi, and others went to the Taihang Mountains to become outlaws in the second year of Xuanhe. This was the earliest group of the thirty-six outlaws, and the location aligns with the official history's origin in Hebei, and the timing may also be credible. Therefore, the time until their failure was just over a year, likely without enough time to establish a base in a mountain stronghold.

Wu Jialiang and six others were the second group to become outlaws, joining Yang Zhi and the twelve others, naturally also going to the Taihang Mountains. Here the name Liangshan Marsh appears, but this Liangshan Marsh is in the Taihang Mountains. Part of the Taihang Mountains was called Liangshan, and the Taihang Mountains were known for having many bandits, which is unnecessary to seek remote evidence that Shandong's Liangshan Marsh was also known for its bandit lairs. The subsequent addition of thirteen more probably also happened in the Taihang Mountains. Later, as their power grew, they roamed through Qi and Wei. Huyan Zhuo and others fought against them without success, and upon joining the group, the number of outlaws reached thirty-six, likely occurring on the way.

If they had a relatively fixed location during their roaming, it was probably in the Huai River basin. The Yuan Dynasty zaju play "Double Contribution" describes Liangshan's terrain as: "The stronghold is named Water Margin, the marsh is called Liangshan; a thousand rivers and harbors crisscross, eight hundred li in all directions; east to the sea, west to Jiyang, south across Juye and Jinxiang, north to Qing, Qi, Yan, and Yun." This already moves Liangshan Marsh to the vicinity described in the later Water Margin, but clearly further south and east. Even if there was not necessarily a suitable area to establish Liangshan Marsh in this region, the author was willing to move Liangshan Marsh to accommodate the story he knew, so it is believable that the location of Liangshan Marsh was more fluid.

Who fixed Liangshan Marsh to Yun Prefecture? Since no one has asked the above question, no one has explored it. I also lack the ability and desire to try to answer the question. It can be vaguely assumed to be the person who wrote the earliest base text for the current version of the Water Margin. Between the Stories of the Xuanhe Era and Luo's Water Margin, there seems to be little room for multiple changes. If there was only one change, then it must have been Shi Nai'an. Based on the content of the Water Margin, the person who wrote this book was likely from western Shandong, not Shi Nai'an from Hangzhou. However, Southern people seem to have their own special legends about Song Jiang, or it is possible that someone from Hangzhou wrote a Song Jiang book that was not the ancestor of the later Water Margin. The relationship between the two is definitely not very close. The book industry in Hangzhou was quite developed at that time, and perhaps when the early version of the Water Margin became popular, Hangzhou also printed it, and the booksellers randomly added the name of a writer known in the local area. This rumor was also spread based on what was recorded in notebooks. (To be continued) Wo Pu

Jottings 199

— Wo Pu

Excerpts from the Four Great Masters' Legends

A collection of miscellaneous dramas from the Qing dynasty, featuring excerpts from the legends of four great masters of prose from the Che Jiang Ying collection. These are divided into the stories of four great masters of ancient prose: Han, Liu, Ou, and Su, namely: "Snow at Lan Pass" (Han), "Mist of Liuzhou" (Liu), "Drunken Pavilion" (Ou), and "Journey to Red Cliff" (Su). All of these use the most popular events in their lives as titles.

Based on my careful reading, I believe that these four pieces are actually legends (chuanqi), not miscellaneous dramas (zaju). Each legend has had several acts extracted and published separately, resembling the nature of selected opera collections. Perhaps they are even unfinished legends, with only a few excerpts released first. (More details below) The term "excerpts" clearly indicates "several extracted acts." The preface by Junyi Sanren says, "Like Xu Wenchang's 'Four Cries of a Gibbon,' it is a rare work from You Zhan Cheng's West Hall Opera House." Although the example given is a zaju, Che's work, like "Four Cries of a Gibbon," combines the stories of Han, Liu, Ou, and Su, similar to how "Peach Blossom Spring" and "Reading Lisao" depict Tao Yuanming and Qu Yuan. One cannot simply use this as evidence that "Excerpts from the Legends of the Four Great Masters" is a zaju or an imitation of Xu and You. There is little doubt that its essence is a legend. A major point of observation is that the themes of each act are inconsistent and full of gaps, lacking cohesion, and the connections are fragmented and incomplete. This is very solid evidence. Below, we will present each one individually.

First, let's look at "Snow at Lan Pass." The theme of this piece should be "Snow Blocking Lan Pass." Shouldn't the legend of Han Xiangzi's attempts to convert Duke Wen be somewhat selected? But Han Xiangzi disappears after returning home to see his wife in the first act, "Return to Xiang." The next acts are (2) "Reporting Shame," depicting Han Yu's appointment to the Huai Xi army; (3) "Enjoying Snow," depicting the capture of Wu Yuanji during a snowy night raid on Caizhou; and (4) "Heng Mountain," depicting Yu ascending Heng Mountain. The story of "Clouds over the Qin Mountains" is not mentioned at all.

The second piece, "Mist of Liuzhou," is very interesting. The author probably still cannot escape the cliché of romance, finding a romance for Liu Zongyuan and Liu Mengde, who both become sons-in-law of Wang Shuwen's family. But the story is still fragmented and incomplete, and we cannot find the concrete unfolding and writing of the true story. (1) "Spring Chamber" introduces Wang Shuwen's two daughters, Wu Ying and Jiu Ying. (2) "Chanting in Response" connects to Liu and Liu passing the imperial examination, receiving silk whips, and going to the Wang family to have the two daughters test their poetry and chant in response. (3) "Folk Songs" depicts Liu's banishment to Lianzhou, hearing of Liu's beautiful administration in Liuzhou. (4) "Post Station Wine Cup" is the grand finale, where Liu, Liu, and Wang's two daughters finally reunite. The incident of the Eight Sima should be the turning point of separation and reunion in the play, with too many gaps and an impossible plot to predict.

In "Drunken Pavilion," the author also fantasizes about a tragic and beautiful romance for him. (1) "Autumn Sound" alludes to the "Autumn Sound Rhapsody." (2) "Reluctant Farewell" depicts Yongshu's farewell to his wife because he is going to the capital to seek fame. This act is completely imitating the "South Pei" from the "Pipa" record. (3) "Mourning Stone" is Yongshu mourning the death of Shi Manqing. (4) "Hibiscus Pavilion" depicts Ouyang's wife, Xu, dying of illness, her soul traveling to the Hibiscus Fairy Pavilion, but Shi Manqing, the lord of the Hibiscus City, takes care of his friend and finds a way to revive her. (5) "Returning Soul" when she wakes up, her husband is away, having "passed the imperial examination and been selected for the literary academy," probably not even knowing his wife was ill? Although the story is absurd, it has no beginning or end, and the events of the Drunken Pavilion are not mentioned. It is likely that the excerpts are mostly from the first half of the legend.

Finally, "Journey to Red Cliff" is the only one that realistically portrays the events indicated by the title. (4) "Red Cliff," (2) "Returning to the Courtyard," depicts the granting of the Golden Lotus by the emperor. The rest (1) "Examining the Son-in-Law," (3) "A Farewell," (5) "Later Meeting," all write about Qin Shaoyou, Su Xiaomei, and the Chu woman Huang Yigu (equivalent to the character Wenjuan or Bian Zhaohua). Like a fragment of the plot from "Ju Mountain Scholar Earns Wenjuan's Love," it is not directly about Dongpo.

What is cited here is only a rough outline. There are various places where the plots of each act are disconnected, but they are still connected by a thread, visible everywhere. All this proves that it is definitely not a complete zaju with four or five acts that has a beginning and an end, nor is each act an independent short play like Jing Shi Shan's "Loose Suite of the Dream of the Red Chamber." In the existing "excerpts," the portrayal of the protagonist is often less than that of other supporting characters (such as Liu Yuxi in "Mist of Liuzhou," and Qin Guan in "Journey to Red Cliff," whose roles are more important and almost equal to Liu and Su). Each of these four pieces should have at least thirty acts or more; otherwise, it would probably not be able to accommodate so many branching, lengthy, complex, and tortuous plot points.

Why did Che want to publish this incomplete piece? Are there complete versions of these four legends? Regarding this point, I suspect that his complete legends have not yet been written; he only has a complete outline and a plan for dividing the acts, and then he is slowly filling in the acts step by step. Perhaps the later acts were done first, not necessarily in order. This is a common experience in writing opera. The phrase "Excerpts from the Filled Lyrics of the Four Great Masters" in the book's seam is worth pondering. As a result, the entire book was never completed, so he made do with what he had and hastily published it, using the word "excerpts" to cover up his shortcomings, perhaps? The fact that the acts are not numbered with "First," "Second," etc. may also be a side proof that they are not complete zaju formats; on the other hand, it may be because the acts in the legends are not fully completed, the order is chaotic, and cannot be determined. Since it is labeled "excerpts," there is no need to hide the original order of the acts. Besides, I cannot think of any other reason why this anthology-style, disconnected "excerpts" would need to be published separately. There seems to be a lack of similar examples of this type of opera collection.

According to Junyi Sanren's preface, Che is from Jiangxi. The year of the preface is Yongzheng Yimao (1735). This is all that is known about his time, place, and life. If half of the above speculation is not true and the four legends are indeed completed, then we will be able to learn more if we are fortunate enough to discover them in the future.

For the sake of the editing style of Qing Dynasty miscellaneous dramas, it would be best to remove it in future reprints, or include it as an appendix, which would be more appropriate. I wonder what the editors and printers think?

Rain (4) 200

— Hewei

He whispered to himself, tears glistening in his eyes. But he was not disappointed, only felt resentment. His uncle and aunt had not come out yet; it must be the old woman who was interfering, not allowing Juanzi to come out with them. Tianli seemed to see Juanzi struggling, pleading, arguing, trying to escape the clutches of that old woman. But that old witch was imprisoning Juanzi, not letting her move a step freely. He thought of the old woman's toothless mouth, that wrinkled face, those fierce and sinister eyes, those dry, corpse-like hands, and suddenly felt a chill all over his body. The white old house also seemed to turn into a gloomy ghost cave in an instant.

He was angry, trembling, only thinking about how Juanzi could live in this environment and how to save her from this kind of life, and unknowingly had already walked to the foot of the ridge.

Just at this moment, he ran into his uncle.

"What, uncle, are you always so oblivious to the world! I've been waiting for you all day; even a trip to the capital should be back by now. How could you..."

"No, no, don't rush!" His uncle, holding a lantern in his hand, hurriedly stopped him.

"Don't rush?"

"Yes, yes, rushing is useless! It's all that hateful old woman; as soon as she heard me talking to Juanzi in a low voice, she came to stop us. And like escorting a prisoner, wherever Juanzi went, she followed. What could I do?"

"So I waited all day in the pavilion, and Juanzi didn't even know?"

"I'm afraid so."

The uncle answered in embarrassment, secretly looking at Tianli's bloodshot eyes burning with fierce fire. Tianli's face was turning ashen, and his hands and feet were trembling as if afraid of the cold.

"How can I be content with this... Fine, let me go find Juanzi myself, and see what that old woman can do to me... Does she think she can eat me? What am I afraid of? ... Uncle ... come with me, let me take the lantern!"

"No, Tianli, why would you want to go and bring bad luck upon yourself?"

The pitiful and weak uncle pleaded in a low voice, but Tianli, having made up his mind, snatched the lantern and ran towards that stone house without looking back, leaving his uncle standing blankly at the dark foot of the ridge, listening to the continuous and mournful sound of the spring rain falling. (The End)

Trivia at Dusk (Part 1) 201

— Shao Guanhua

Dragging my tired legs, I boarded the motorboat; with a "whoosh," the boat set off immediately. The waves cradled the boat, trembling, drifting from this shore to that shore in just fifteen minutes.

Ornate silk ribbons were tied to bamboo poles on the shore, and dozens of electric lights shone brightly, adding to the energy of the dusk.

I had to go to the ×× Hall for some trivial matters, which made my heart even more lonely.

My legs were still tired, so I called for a rickshaw.

—Rickshaw, ×× Hall!

—Three hundred cash.

—Two hundred and forty.

After confirming the deal, I placed myself on the rickshaw, following the route the rickshaw was taking, my body being moved along.

The elderly rickshaw puller perked up, pulling the rickshaw and running along the dilapidated city edge.

The ground was covered with dirt, with small, sharp stones standing on it. The rickshaw moved over these two materials, bumping almost as much as the sedan chairs I often passed through in the countryside of × county in Jiangnan.

Upon arriving at the ×× Hall, I finished the things I needed to do and came out. My legs were even more tired, so I had to sit in the rickshaw. I went to ×× Road to buy some odds and ends.

The wind gently blew on my shoulders, and I suddenly woke up from my fatigue. Looking ahead, I realized that the rickshaw puller was dragging me to another road.

Low, flat houses stood on both sides of the road the rickshaw was dragging through. Kerosene lamps were placed on wooden tables in each house, emitting the same weak light in different directions. Once the rickshaw had passed, the darkness of the starless dusk enveloped the front again.

—It's so hard to walk here, the rickshaw puller said.

—Who told you to pull here in this dark place? Couldn't you have taken the other road? It's just a little further, I said.

—Hmm.

So I reached into my pocket, took out a flashlight, and rubbed it. Its light shone five feet ahead of the rickshaw.

—Good, the rickshaw puller shouted again.

Relying on the not-so-bright light of the flashlight, I could vaguely see a small wall, and in front of the wall, a few newly sprouted willow trees were planted, revealing a child-like breath.

Two minutes later, the rickshaw moved me in another direction. The black iron gates closed the slightly tidy house number. Under the electric light, ×× Lane No. 15 was quite clearly visible.

Rambling Talk on Willpower and Other Things, to Brother Mo Fei 202

— Yang Sao

Brother Mo Fei:

I am now staying in N City again, living with Brother Dan, temporarily being a big parasite. Today, from the letter you sent to Brother Dan, I know that you are still concerned about my job problem. I felt a sense of warmth between people for a moment, and this prompted me to fulfill the desire to write you a letter that I have long had. However, when I pick up the pen, I don't know what to write. Let me just say some empty words.

The older a person gets, unless the harsh environment makes them truly senile and unwilling or unable to think, their understanding of all phenomena—natural and human—will naturally become more profound and accurate. Therefore, there are many examples, both ancient and modern, of people who initially could not understand each other, or even opposed and devoured each other, eventually becoming harmonious or embracing under a completely consistent view after the passage of time. A person's emotions, willpower, and consciousness are undoubtedly determined by their physiological state and, more importantly, their circumstances. I remember arguing with you on the upper floor of a certain newspaper office about the question of free will. At that time, you were a believer in free will, and I was exactly the opposite. In the past year or two, I don't know if your view has changed? I am completely the same as before, that is, I do not believe in free will. Moreover, the life experience of the past year or two has strengthened my belief. I believe that the barriers between people are extremely thin and easily torn apart, caused by differences in physiology and circumstances. If this membrane, which is not divinely ordained—there is no divinely ordained phenomenon in the universe—but is easily changeable or transformable, is pierced, and two people have relatively similar living environments, and thus have relatively similar emotions, intellect, and consciousness, then the two people can definitely be friends. Is it that you were born to like to eat rice, and I am destined to eat wheat and oppose you? Is it that Brother Dan brought a Hamlet-type personality from his mother's womb, and Mr. He's arrogance was given by God? No, definitely not! Your willingness to eat rice is cultivated by the tradition that China produces a lot of rice and that Chinese people eat rice. I originally ate rice too, but my stomach disease determined that I must eat wheat. Furthermore, Brother Dan's Hamlet-type personality and Mr. He's arrogance each have their own reasons, each caused by their respective living environments. Moreover, these characteristics, emotions, wishes, willpower, etc., which are slowly created by the living environment, are not solidified and unchangeable. They will change with the changes in the living environment. Therefore, the hatred and misunderstanding between people will not be permanent, and it is possible for people to shake hands and walk the same path. Also for this reason, the phenomenon of in-laws becoming mortal enemies is extremely natural and often makes us see it, making us feel sad.

These rigid and superficial words will definitely make you smile, and there is really no need to say them. However, if I think about wanting to let you know that I am now much more optimistic than before because of this more solid understanding of this shallow recognition, I should not be afraid of you laughing at my shallowness and say it. Do you know, from this deeper understanding of the non-freedom of emotions and willpower, I have reduced a lot of sadness for all kinds of helpless separations, and increased infinite hope for the various barriers that cannot be brought together now. Therefore, I feel lighter; I feel that I am not oppressed by nostalgia and disappointment, and my future is bright! Walking along the right path, I will have many companions along the way. Although some are destined to leave me or abandon me, new ones will continue to come. I will never be alone, as long as I do not avoid the current society out of disgust. Yes, this society, its form, its direction, and people's willpower and emotions, like the people's will and emotions, also change due to the changes in the various institutions that organize it, and it is changing every moment. I cannot live optimistically in this constantly moving society and let the environment determine my actions. Then why should I be sad, sentimental, disappointed, and depressed? Everything is not accidental. I can recognize the inevitable, and if I set my destiny on the path of the inevitable, then I'm done!

I babbled a lot of nonsense, and I don't even know where this nonsense came from. I think it must have its source, but I don't feel it myself. I guess that this nonsense may even make you criticize me for becoming a mechanical person, because I seem to have no willpower at all, because I completely deny free will. However, let me declare in advance that this is not the case. I have not and cannot become a mechanical person. That's right, I completely deny the "freedom" of willpower, but I do not deny the "effect" of willpower. I still have willpower. Perhaps this can comfort a friend who is still concerned about my job problem overseas.

I have been in N City for nearly a month, and I have not done anything, nor have I written any articles. I am really a little worried. My job is of course hanging in mid-air; it will not fall down by itself unless I flap my wings and dance to take it. But in any case, I will reasonably strive to live from now on. I will not have as much trouble as before, with few smiles, too much sentimental behaviour, and not enough masculinity, making my friends uncomfortable to see.

I hope you can communicate often when you have time. Please give my regards to your wife. Aren't you about to raise a child? And I wish your future little treasure health!

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Banning Coeducation in Middle Schools 203

— Xing An

Beijing, a city with ancient culture, has recently been banning coeducation in middle schools. According to a Beijing dispatch on the 25th, the ban on coeducation in municipal middle schools in Beijing has been implemented. Now the municipal government has issued another order banning coeducation in private middle schools. All must comply from this summer onwards in order to maintain morality.

The practice of coeducation in our country has been around for several years. Now, why is the Beijing authorities suddenly issuing an order to ban it? According to the declaration in the Beijing Municipal Government's ban, the purpose of banning coeducation in middle schools is "to maintain morality." From this perspective, it seems that the Beijing education community, which has practiced coeducation for several years, has probably already discovered some incidents related to morality in the past. Therefore, the Beijing authorities are now issuing an order to ban it in order to prevent the continued occurrence of such incidents. If this guess is correct, then the Beijing authorities' issuance of an order to ban coeducation in middle schools this time is commendable for its painstaking effort. Otherwise, Beijing's ban is a bit too abrupt. What's being sold in this gourd is probably something else.

Can middle schools practice coeducation? This question really doesn't need to be discussed anymore. What we need to pay attention to here is whether coeducation in middle schools will hinder morality. This is the point. Those who oppose coeducation in middle schools have always argued that young people are at a time of maturity during their middle school years. Contact between men and women often leads to free love affairs, so they advocate that men and women should not be in the same school. This reason seems to be right but is not. It must be understood that coeducation is one thing, and free love is another. Does banning coeducation prevent free love affairs between young men and women? Taking a step back, it is inevitable that free love will occur between young men and women in coeducation. But is this a mysterious period for young men and women that can be forcibly prohibited? If it is said that young men and women should strive to learn and pursue knowledge during their middle school years, and if they embark on the path of free love, there is a risk of neglecting their studies, then it is better for middle schools to be segregated. This sounds very reasonable. But we have to ask, does banning coeducation prevent young people from free love? Then, if young men and women who are generally in segregated schools also engage in free love, will this neglect their studies?

Taking another step back, it is because of coeducation that young people engage in free love. But is it immoral for young men and women to engage in free love? No, right? If it is said that legitimate free love between young men and women is also harmful to morality, then there are really too many such immoral things in society. Even if the authorities want to maintain it, they will feel that there is no way to maintain it.

However, the Beijing authorities are now issuing an order to ban coeducation in middle schools. We really cannot figure out what morality there is to maintain in coeducational middle schools.

Old Classmate 204

— Hua Zhi

The weariness of life often leads me to sit alone under the lamp, gazing at the sky dotted with stars. Time, like that, flies by without the slightest hesitation. One evening, rain drizzled outside the window, and the sky was a blurry haze. The land of freedom where my eyes usually roamed was now shifted to the naked portrait hanging on the wall. The days passed even faster in my memory. As I was about to vow to cherish my future again, a gentle sound of leather shoes echoed from the stairs, the sound clearly directed towards my room. Hearing an unfamiliar voice, as refined as a woman’s, asking for my name, I felt as though I had been waiting for this uninvited guest. When I opened the door, the lamplight

Page 18

shone onto the face of the visitor, and I quickly thought of a polite greeting to offer him.

The visitor had a slender figure, paired with a thin face. Underneath a mess of disheveled hair, his disarray was even more apparent. Because I was standing with my back to the light, the visitor hesitated slightly, just as I was taking him in. Then, an overwhelming joy made him exclaim:

"Old friend, I never thought we’d meet again!"

He tightly grasped my hand at the same time. In my bewilderment, I was awakened by the fiery gaze in his eyes. It was my old classmate, Xu Jun.

After graduating from a county school in the countryside, I went to Shanghai to attend university. I was not accustomed to the surrounding environment and often confined myself to the dormitory like a bookworm. Xu Jun was my roommate. He was a modern college student, well-versed in all sorts of university pastimes. For example, he knew various dance steps. When he walked across the lawn like a gentleman, he whistled popular songs. As for sports, he was the target of all the school beauties. I cannot describe him in detail; in short, he and I were too far apart. Perhaps there were times when we didn’t even meet. I don't know if he looked down on me, but our incompatibility was an undeniable fact.

Such a modern youth—when I stepped out of the school gates and was whipped by the realities of life, if it weren't for the familiar gaze I once dared not meet, I wouldn't have believed that the person now holding my hand was Xu Jun from back then.

After we sat down, he used his sharp eyes to survey my bedroom. Although we were not as estranged as we were in the dormitory, he still felt that this dilapidated building was not fitting for welcoming a dear classmate whom he hadn’t seen in so long. But he said:

"The situation is very good!"

He pulled a cigarette from the tin and smiled as if in envy. This made me feel even more ashamed, regardless of whether he was mocking me or not. I turned the writing chair to face away from the light, thinking of some opening remarks to politely respond to him, but no matter how hard I tried, I just couldn't come up with the words. He lit the cigarette, walked over, and gently patted my shoulder, showing a kind of American-style familiarity, while pacing around the room with small steps.

"How has life been these past few years?" I finally asked him.

He immediately stopped and repeated my question, "Good!"

"I heard you’re doing quite well!" he laughed like a tiger. "This time, I came back from Nanjing and met Old Wang on the train. He told me you’ve been doing very well recently."

Looking at his sincere attitude, I couldn’t suspect that he was mocking me, but what could I say to satisfy him?

"Old friend, please keep an eye out for opportunities for me," he finally said, uttering the words I had already guessed.

I nodded subconsciously, looking into my old classmate’s probing eyes.

Son 205

— Ling Zixi

From the time when Sister-in-law Jin told a few gossipy women at the riverbank about the news in the morning, by noon, almost everyone in this small village of only about twenty families was talking about the same thing: "The woman that Genfu newly married has been going out every night for the past three days!"

The person who talked about this the most enthusiastically and described it most vividly was Sister-in-law Jin, who lived next door to Genfu. She had started "keeping tabs" on Genfu's wife (since Sister-in-law Jin’s suggestion, no one in the village called the newly arrived woman "Genfu's wife"!) from the moment "Genfu's wife" entered Genfu's house in a small red sedan chair amidst the playing of the three drummers and Taoist priests hired from the Daoshi Temple above Banpo. The reasons were there: Genfu worked in Shanghai, leaving an old mother at home, and her meals and other needs were all taken care of by Sister-in-law Jin for six silver dollars a month. Now that Genfu had brought back a wife, this business would certainly not be successful. Secondly, it was said that the "new bride" had no manners. She didn’t even call Sister-in-law Jin "Auntie Jin" when she made her greetings. So, after three days, Sister-in-law Jin used an odd tone to shout in the ears of Genfu's half-deaf mother: "Your good daughter-in-law is worth a lot, with her oily hair and bright face, she’s worth a lot! Hmph, hmph!"

And, after seeing Genfu's wife sneaking out of the back door for three nights in a row, the first person to tell everyone else about it would of course be none other than Sister-in-law Jin. "Hmph! I told you all a long time ago: a woman with oily hair and a bright face, without roots or support, can’t be a good sort! ... Every night, she always goes out with her hair slicked back and her face shiny; and when she comes back, the way she looks is... Oh my... you haven't seen it yet (in fact, even Sister-in-law Jin herself had never seen what she looked like when she came back). Oh my... it’s sickening! How can this kind of thing endure it when Genfu is working outside for months at a time! There will be more jokes later, you watch and see..."

In fact, it was true that Genfu's wife had been secretly going out every night recently, but it was not necessarily true that she had "no roots or support": when people "arranged" for this woman to marry Genfu, they also asked matchmakers to write a "marriage agreement". She was a pretty little widow from the next village over, and she had no one else in her family. Originally, she didn’t want to remarry, but her husband had died, and she didn’t have enough to eat, so..."

Genfu's own wife had been dead for two years, and his old mother at home needed someone to take care of her; and he himself was always working in Shanghai. It would be good to have a family, even if he could only come back once or twice a month. So, taking advantage of the fact that he had some money on hand, he spent fifty silver dollars to get a "clean and tidy" wife.

However, at the very moment when the story of "Genfu's wife going out every night..." was spreading throughout the village, Genfu also heard the rumors from his fellow villagers in Shanghai, and secretly came back with a fiery murderous intent. On the first night, he silently squatted in the dark corner that Sister-in-law Jin had arranged, and watched as the woman went out as usual at night, then quietly followed her!

Having already crossed to the next village, Genfu's wife, as if carrying a kind of urgent longing, immediately entered a half-closed door.

Inside the door, there were children's laughter and women's laughter: "Good child, good child, be good. If it weren’t for you, Mommy would have followed your dead dad long ago..."

It was already more than he could bear. As if having gone mad, Genfu burst through the door and dragged the woman out: "Good for you, you big whore!" And then, by the time he dragged her home, he had already beaten her half to death. "If it wasn’t for this son, if it wasn’t for..." All the woman could say was these few words.

Half a month later, Genfu did not return, and everyone in the village also knew that Genfu's wife had a son in the village ahead; but when some of the women began to forgive her, Genfu’s wife had already hanged herself on a tree branch in front of the door.

Professor Reduces Price 206

Withering Flower 207

— Rong

Those who have never been married see marriage as a vibrant flower, its fragrance rich, its posture alluring, as elegant as a magnolia in the morning mist, as passionate as a rose entwined with summer lightning, as mellow as a drunken hibiscus leaning lazily on green leaves. But this childish fantasy is just like a fresh flower; once crushed by the iron fist of reality, it immediately withers and dries up.

In my memory, which is covered with the dust of years, there is a spring that will never disappear. It may be a flower that withered and faded after releasing its color and fragrance, but its sweet scent lingers forever in my nostrils, comforting my whole body. I cannot forget that April day with its gentle breeze. It was a myth, a long and melodious love song.

When the sky was piled high with clouds of purplish bronze, and the ground was adorned with lush green grass, two children ran out of their homes without restraint, running from the fields to the water's edge, where they rested. The water's edge was covered with thousands of yellow wildflowers and scarlet azaleas. Cuckoos sang of the rich wheat harvest in the fields. Separated only by a shallow stream, one could hear the sound of fishermen splashing water with their spears and casting their nets. In the setting sun, the green mountains took on a touch of purple. It was extremely pleasant to have two children pouring out their innocent and mysterious souls in this environment. Their clear laughter and the natural world formed a single pulse. Those two children were me and Caiqing.

"So, if Auntie wants to marry you off, what will you do?"

"That doesn't matter. I've already agreed to her."

"But you'll have to raise children, and you'll be beaten by your in-laws, understand?"

Hearing these words, she turned her head and said, "I'm not afraid."

"My mom also wants to find me a wife, saying I'm too young, not yet..."

The two children talked tirelessly, exchanging all sorts of conversations about themselves and their future happiness. "The future" was like an extremely magnificent drawing in front of us, a radiant glow of colorful clouds. Hope filled everyone's hearts, just as fruits and grains filled the granaries. In our dreams, a long period of days slipped by. At that time, she was still sixteen years old, and I was studying. A year later, she got married. She began to embark on the endless arduous path of life, like a traveler walking a long way, even her last shadow disappearing into the darkness. I haven't seen her since. I have been using fatigue and endurance to pass my years. That's how I spent many years.

Like swallows in spring, we met again this year. She was yellow and haggard, like a middle-aged woman. With her were a group of cumbersome children and a thin husband. In just a few years, time had relentlessly sculpted her into another statue, all stiff and prosaic. The impression she gave me was of dusk, an uninhabited temple, outdated newspapers, a lonely autumn garden. Facing this vulgarized shell, I was astonished by the dramatic changes that had occurred in the past few years. I couldn't believe my own eyes. I thought of the dreams of the past, the poetic longing for marriage, the beautiful spring fields, the sound of cuckoos echoing on the mountain cliffs and water's edge, and the small mountain flowers. Finally, these things quickly collapsed, and a dark fog covered all my fantasies...

We spent an afternoon in the park. Spring had already passed, and the sun was unbearably scorching. The wilderness only showed a dreary green color. As we walked over a small bridge, a withering flower fell onto my shoulder, into my sleeve. Finally, I brushed it off onto the ground with my handkerchief...

"That's a withered flower!" I said quietly.

Her face looked a little strange. She said, "This is just like, a person..." She didn't finish the second half of the sentence.

I also had nothing to say. I only looked at the flower once. The flower had already been engulfed by the dark soil.

Family Letter 208

— Tianzhen

Who says "A letter from home is worth ten thousand gold?"! As for me, I feel a kind of terror, as afraid of it as of a ferocious tiger. Yet the cover is clearly adorned with the claw marks of my nurturer. The unkempt merchant's handwriting is so familiar to me, so intimate, and two years of longing wind around me, tempt me. Finally, I couldn't help but tremble as I tore it open.

Nothing surprises me at all. My nerves seem to have been tamed by the surprising things that the era has refined. Emotions are burned into ashes and seeped into the dust of the universe. Even if a towering stone mountain collapsed on my mind, it wouldn't seem to stir up the slightest ripple. As numb as a stubborn stone! That's what I thought.

However, no, I also know very clearly: two sheets of eight-line paper are a sketch of family affairs over two years. A few brief strokes are so profound, so lifelike, so sad and moving. But I feel that I still have a bit of the primitive numbness; otherwise, how could I even cherish my tears of blood, unwilling to shed a single drop?

However, I also remember very clearly: an autumn evening two years ago, my father's face, making one's tears fall for three days.

Page 19

It was the first time we had met in six years. He looked at me with a stunned expression, and I also had the sincerity of "laughingly asking, where do you come from?". Each of us wisely touched the other's soul. Only then did he begin to ask with a stranger's air:

"I'm old! I didn't expect that we father and son would have a chance to meet!"

He narrowed his eyes, and several rainbows hung diagonally on the green edge of his pupils. With dew-like moistness, they reached his shriveled, blackened lower lip.

A breath of mint slowly spread across my heart. The path of words was blocked by clear tears. A son's aging is not easily spoken by a father, oh! That "old" word carrying ten million pounds, made all the hairs on my body fall upside down, and the brain cells exceeded the weight of my whole body!

"You're even more aged!" I became as terrified as if I were about to be executed by a blade.

In more than sixty years of the journey of life, his history had his golden age, the time when he sat at the exchange, the time when he operated two storefronts, the time when he manipulated finance. His plump physique symbolized his smooth path in the world. People envied the "God of Wealth", followed him, and longed for him. He was able to show a unique alertness and decisiveness in everything. He did not expect that a desolate shadow would envelop his old age! Mentioning the creation of his later history, he seemed to grieve for himself for no reason. Because of this, I am even more frightened that my sins will never be redeemed. The son, he, like ordinary people, had great fantasies. For these fantasies, he once cherished me with rare passion, irrigated me, until now he has fallen into the eyes of the world, but still retains his original foolish energy. Standing in front of him, can I still have the qualification to be high-spirited?

The words seemed to have been completely answered and concluded from the intersecting lines of sight: I had an awkward appearance, and he had a withered leaf-like face intertwined with sorrow and joy.

In the evening, he stayed in my small room, which cost eight silver dollars a month, and slept on the same bed.

As usual, even friends should exchange a few pleasantries in a silent face-to-face, but precisely because they are friends, there is the mood for pleasantries. At present, pressing on each other's mood is a strand of inexplicable sadness. No one needs to say anything, as if a layer of forbidden net has been laid down in front of them; they silently wait for the sleeping devil to swallow up each person's sensitivity and wit.

However, the sleeping devil is not as kind as we imagined—a single quilt suddenly became huge. I reached out and touched it, and my father's feet were exposed outside. I immediately understood that my father still had the same mentality as before: fearing that I would catch a cold, he let me cover myself more. I covered his feet with the quilt, and he seemed uncomfortable. After a while, he gently turned over, as if afraid of disturbing me, and his hand touched from my ankle to my upper thigh. Releasing his hand, he let out a sigh of heartache that I had heard often at home, and there seemed to be a muttering sound from his mouth.

"Dad, is the bed too narrow? Is it uncomfortable to sleep?" I asked what was wrong.

"It's not that! I felt only a few bones left on your thigh! Buy some ginseng to eat!"

After a moment of heartache, I prepared to say: We don't even have food to eat, and you want to eat ginseng! But I was afraid of hurting his heart, and in the end, I dared not say it. Deception is an unforgivable sin, but stimulating his pain with the truth is also a kind of cruelty. In the end, I could only say, "Yes, yes, yes," to appease his wishes.

Now that I have read his letter, his silver beard and withered leaf face have surfaced in my mind again. I wish I could tear it and my heart to pieces together.

Movie News

"Metropolitan Scenery" to Begin Filming 214

The detailed shooting script for Yuan Muzhi's fourth film, "Metropolitan Scenery", is already complete and filming will begin soon. Shen Bao Local Supplement: Automobile Weekly

Projected Number of Cars Made in the US This Year 221

— Yu

The Factory Target is Three and a Half Million Vehicles; New Cars for Next Year Will Debut Early in November

American automakers recently reviewed the national car production volume for the first quarter of this year. The number of cars manufactured by various factories reached 1,000,000 vehicles. By the third quarter of this year, in the first six months, American car production should reach at least 2,000,000 vehicles. The automakers' target for the whole year's production volume is 3,500,000 vehicles, or even more. In terms of quantity, the second quarter should be greater than the first quarter. For the remaining period, it will continue according to President Roosevelt's plan. All the new cars of 1936 will debut about two months early, which will have a significant impact on the increase in the annual production volume. The original intention of this plan is to allow workers to obtain more work throughout the twelve months. The date of the new car launch will be moved from January 1st to November 1st. The heads of various companies also mostly advocate advancing the auto show to early November. The New York Auto Show is also planned to be hosted by the companies to replace the one initiated by the sales agents in 1935.

Whether the automotive industry can reach the target of 5,500,000 vehicles is uncertain, and avoiding major delays is essential. Car body and parts manufacturing are not currently caught in the vortex of strikes. Other departments are often threatened by strikes due to worker agitation. The Akron plant's tire department is also in danger of shutting down. Recent reports indicate that the upcoming eight-day work system tends to be postponed. During this period, elections are being held at the Goodyear, Firestone, and Goodrich plants.

In the first three months of this year, in the production of over 1,000,000 cars, Chrysler's five products, Plymouth, DeSoto, Dodge, Chrysler, and Fargo, reached a total of 249,064 units for both passenger cars and trucks, which is an unprecedented achievement for the factory. During this quarter, Plymouth shipped a total of 136,040 units. The factories in Detroit and Los Angeles are manufacturing approximately 2,000 cars per day.

In the General Motors division, Pontiac's quarterly output was 51,809 passenger cars. The output for February was 17,802 units. The factory's production plan for April has reached 19,000 units. Walter P. Chrysler's production by March 30 totaled 44,441 units. This number is the highest record for the factory's output, so the weekly production volume has reached 4,500 vehicles.

After a year of organizational effort, the Society of Automotive Engineers has developed a new standard for the steel used in automobile manufacturing to "match" the specialized uses of automobiles. To accomplish this task, 29 metallurgical experts, representatives from factories related to steel and automobile manufacturing, collaborated and studied each other.

Export department staff members of the factories belonging to the American Automobile Manufacturers Association recently held a regular meeting in New York to discuss the expansion of overseas sales. Among them, Mr. Bowie, a long-time overseas representative of the American automotive industry, reported on the issue of tax reduction for American car exports, and that reciprocity arrangements have been negotiated with seventeen foreign countries. Bowie also said that the government has reached an understanding with the Belgian authorities that American cars imported into that country will be subject to a 15% reduction in the existing tax rate. When this is implemented, there will be opportunities for three other countries to reduce taxes on American-made cars. The United States will also similarly reduce tax rates on imports from these countries in exchange. Other countries still under negotiation include Italy, Sweden, Canada, some Central American republics, and Haiti. Some foreign countries have a clause on American car imports that all American cars transported by ship must be shipped in boxes. This regulation affects the cost of transporting cars from the factory to the port, increasing it by about 13%. Bowie and his collaborators are currently working to change this regulation so that cars not packaged can also be accepted for transportation by shipping companies.

The First Marius Arriving in Shanghai Seventeen Years Ago 222

— Fu

The Machinery is Still Excellent and Intact

The date of the first Marius car arriving in Shanghai was actually seventeen years ago. At that time, the Central Garage accepted the car as it was the Marius dealer at the time. This car is still running normally today. The machinery is still excellent and intact, without any flaws. Mr. Greenback, the business manager of Ardian Trading Co., Ltd., said to people after the first batch of new Marius cars arrived in Shanghai: "Let us look at the amazing effectiveness of this first Marius, the strong sales in Shanghai after its debut, the enthusiastic welcome from the people of Shanghai, and the urgent need for it. We can know that the business policy that Marius has set is well-considered and impeccable." In these seventeen years, although the automotive industry has undergone various changes, Marius still insists on the basic conditions that it set when it first manufactured the first car. According to the founder of Marius, the purpose of manufacturing cars is to ensure that car owners do not waste a single penny and can enjoy extreme reliability. They believe that to achieve this kind of reliability, it is necessary to have sound design, excellent material selection, and sophisticated technology. Having clearly identified the goal and being able to persevere, its products are the same as the first Marius. The service is absolutely satisfactory, and the life span is doubled. The so-called maintenance and operation can obtain the greatest service at the lowest cost.

Dodge's Old Workers Participate in the Ceremony for the Three Millionth Dodge Car to Leave the Factory 223

According to the well-known manager of Dodge cars in Shanghai, China Motor Corporation, the company recently received news from the factory that the three millionth Dodge car was completed the other day. At the time, more than 20 old workers who were initially hired by the factory and have been there ever since participated in the ceremony. Most of them have silver hair, but their spirits are very energetic. They were all excited and comforted by the birth of this car. Because they had personally built the first Dodge more than 20 years ago, and now they have witnessed the birth of the three millionth car, which is excellent and reliable, and has reached the realm of perfection, their heartfelt joy is multiplied compared to ordinary people. The average age of these old workers is 66 years old, and their average years of service is 23 and a half years. When the first Dodge was assembled, only 12 people participated, but within a week, the number increased to 100, and the output reached 25 vehicles per day. Today, 20 years later, the output of Dodge passenger cars alone has reached 1,000 vehicles per day, and about 25,000 employees are employed. The picture above is the three millionth Dodge.

Economical Use of Storage Batteries 224

— Ren

The importance of storage batteries in the automotive industry is beyond doubt. Everyone acknowledges it. But how to use a storage battery so that it lasts a long time without being damaged is a major issue from an economic point of view. If the following points are paid attention to, the problem of economical use will not be difficult to solve.

(1) Charging must follow the specified rate. The standard specified time for ordinary lead-acid batteries is eight hours. If charging can be done according to this specified time, the battery's efficiency and effective life will definitely achieve good results. In addition, faster or slower is not appropriate, especially faster is the most harmful. Because the time is short, if you still want to reach a certain amount of power storage (ampere-hours), the number of amperes of current must be increased. As a result, the released bubbles are both fast and numerous, and the temperature rises, so that the effective material does not have time to adhere to the lead sheet and is inadvertently left at the bottom of the battery, causing a short circuit. The extent of the danger is not difficult to imagine.

(2) Electrolyte specific gravity limit. No matter what the degree of charging or discharging, it can be measured with a hydrometer. During charging, the specific gravity of the electrolyte is between 1.200 and 1.300. During discharging, the specific gravity of the electrolyte must not exceed 1.170.

(3) Do not overcharge. Under the specified charging rate, whether the battery's charging level is satisfactory can be determined by the following three methods.

First. The battery voltage does not increase within one hour.

Second. A large number of bubbles are generated between the two poles of the battery, like boiling.

Third. The specific gravity of the electrolyte remains conservative within one hour, without increase or decrease.

(4) Do not over-discharge. Over-discharge can cause the amount of lead sulfate precipitated to increase sharply. However, because lead sulfate is a poor conductor, the internal resistance increases and the voltage decreases. Eventually, the sulfuric acid also suddenly hardens, causing the main objects in the battery to collapse and fall off. Therefore, the ills of over-discharge must be carefully avoided. Under the specified discharge rate, ordinary batteries should stop discharging when the voltage drops to 1.750 volts. (Continued on page 10)

(5) The electrolyte must be pure. The sulfuric acid and distilled water used in the electrolyte should be as pure as possible to obtain the highest efficiency. Impure electrolytes, such as those containing other metal impurities, etc., if accumulated on the electrode plates, will have a local effect on the lead plates, consuming a lot of electrical energy, which is not suitable for economic use.

(6) Pay attention to the positive and negative poles of the power supply when charging. If the positive and negative poles of the power supply are not clearly marked, it is easy to make mistakes. If you are not careful and make a mistake, not only will it not be able to charge, but it will also cause the lead sulfate to harden and other main objects to collapse and fall off. A simple method for testing the positive and negative poles of the power supply is to take a bottle of diluted salt water and pass the positive and negative poles of the power supply through it. The pole that can generate bubbles in the salt water is undoubtedly the cathode.

(7) Storage method when the battery is not in use. If the battery is not in use, it must be fully charged before being stored. The location should also be cool and dry. If the electrolyte is slightly reduced due to evaporation, distilled water should be added to replenish it. Make sure that the electrolyte level is about half an inch above the top of the electrode plates.
